Conducting Post-War Relief in the War Zone 27

The Two Committees Hold Meetings One After Another

The Preparatory Committee for Post-War Relief in the Songhu War Zone has been organized and established after the 31st meeting of the Executive Yuan of the National Government resolved to appoint Song Ziwen and other 18 people as members. Details about the committee are recorded below.

Order of the Executive Yuan 28

The Executive Yuan instructed the Post-War Relief Committee in the Songhu War Zone, saying: "In order to make an order, since the Shanghai Incident occurred, the areas within the war zone, such as Zhabei, Wusong, Jiangwan, and Liuhe, have been severely damaged, especially the losses of the people. Now that the war has come to an end, post-war relief should be properly planned. The organization of the Preparatory Committee for Post-War Relief in the Songhu War Zone is hereby made, and members are appointed. It should be established immediately and planned. All matters concerning the investigation of losses and the restoration of the market should be properly planned by the committee and submitted for approval and implementation."

Committee Meeting 29

The committee convened its first committee meeting on the 18th of this month. Song Ziwen, Wu Tiecheng, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Shi Liangcai, Zhang Gongquan, Lu Jianquan, Qin Runqing, Hu Junzhuang, Hu Zhangjiang, Li Yi, and other eleven people attended. Chairman Song Ziwen presided over the meeting and discussed various ways to proceed in detail. It is now heard that the second committee meeting will be convened on the 21st to conduct further discussions.

Shanghai City 30

The Post-War Rehabilitation Committee for the War Zone is organized by the Shanghai Special Municipal Government. In addition to the Mayor, Municipal Government Counselors, the Secretary-General, and the Directors of various bureaus being ex-officio members, the remaining members are appointed by the Mayor from local figures. The designated candidates are as follows:

Designated Candidates 31

Shi Liangcai, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Gongquan, Chen Guangfu, Qin Runqing, Li Ming, Liu Hongsheng, Wang Yiting, Chen Bingqian, Guo Shun, Du Yuesheng, Shen Tianxin, Wang Binyan, (Zhabei) Tang Chengzong, (Wusong) Wu Xuen, (Jiangwan) Hong Lanxiang, (Zhenru) [missing character] You, (Yinxiang) Invitation letters will be sent out in the coming days.

Organizational Rules for the Shanghai Municipal War Zone Post-War Rehabilitation Committee: Article 1: The Shanghai Municipal Government, in order to gather ideas and actively plan for the post-war rehabilitation of the disaster areas within the city, organizes the Shanghai Municipal War Zone Post-War Rehabilitation Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee"). Article 2: The Committee's scope of deliberation is as follows: (1) Matters concerning public security and guards in the disaster areas; (2) Matters concerning refugee relief in the disaster areas; (3) Matters concerning public health and epidemic prevention in the disaster areas; (4) Matters concerning public utilities in the disaster areas; (5) Matters concerning construction work in the disaster areas; (6) Matters concerning education in the disaster areas; (7) Matters concerning land consolidation in the disaster areas. Article 3: The Committee shall have twenty members. In addition to the Mayor, Counselors, Secretary-General, and the Directors of various bureaus being ex-officio members, the remaining members shall be appointed by the Mayor from local figures. Article 4: The Chairman of the Committee shall be concurrently held by the Mayor. The Vice-Chairman shall be elected from among the appointed members. Article 5: The Committee may appoint specialist members and assign staff members. Article 6: Committee members shall serve without pay. However, specialist members and staff members may be reimbursed for travel expenses as appropriate. Article 7: The Committee shall hold a regular meeting once a week. The date shall be determined by the meeting. In the event of important incidents, the Chairman may convene extraordinary meetings. Article 8: The Committee may work in groups. Detailed rules for work will be determined separately. Article 9: Matters not covered by these rules may be amended at any time. Article 10: These rules shall come into effect from the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

No Troops Stationed in Southern Wusong 32

The Joint Association Resolves to Question Luo Wengan

Results of Dispatching Personnel to Inspect Longhua

The Shanghai All-Circles National Salvation Joint Association, based on newspaper reports that the Longhua Garrison Headquarters had stationed Chinese soldiers, dispatched Yang Youren, an executive member of the Association, to Longhua the day before yesterday to inspect whether there were any troops stationed there. After the executive member reported to the Board of Directors, the Standing Board of Directors held a meeting yesterday afternoon to discuss the report. They found that the Garrison Department did not have any soldiers stationed there, and considered this situation proof that the so-called "no troops stationed in Southern Wusong" had evidently become a reality. They then resolved to issue a circular telegram in opposition and to question Foreign Minister Luo Wengan. The report of the executive member on the situation in Longhua is recorded below: Report: Having been dispatched to the Longhua Garrison Headquarters to observe whether there were any formal Chinese troops stationed there, I drove to the gate of the Headquarters at 10:00 a.m. on May 19th. The two guards at the gate were wearing cloth military uniforms and holding rifles, but were members of the 2nd squad of the factory guard of the Ordnance Factory. Entering the gate to the Garrison Headquarters office, there were two police officers from the 2nd company of the Municipal Public Security Police Brigade standing guard at the entrance, holding Mauser pistols. I was introduced by Mr. Li Cishan and presented my and Mr. Wu Gao's, the Secretary of the Headquarters, name cards, which were handed to a messenger wearing a plain, evergreen [missing character] serge uniform. I also wrote a visitor's slip (the visitor's slip book stated "Twenty-first year of the Republic, May, one book, total of five sheets used"). The messenger took the card inside. I remained waiting in the messenger's room. Shortly afterwards, the messenger came out and said, "Secretary Xie is not in. It is uncertain when he will come. You can come back another day when he is here." His tone seemed evasive. I then presented the card of the All-Circles National Salvation Joint Association and stated that I had been dispatched to investigate the troop stationing situation. If Secretary Xie was not in, could I ask the Adjutant to meet with me? Today's newspapers had a statement from Adjutant Chen Letian of the Headquarters. If this was true, I might as well ask to see Adjutant Chen." The messenger actually said, "Newspaper reports are not reliable. Although there is an Adjutant Chen at the Headquarters, there is no one named Letian." I further inquired whether the troops currently stationed in the department were officers of the Public Security Bureau Police Brigade, and he replied, "Yes, I suppose so." He also said, "The Commander has not come to the department to work and it is uncertain when he will come." After repeated questioning by myself, the messenger ran out of arguments and excuses, and even if I continued to press him, he would not give a responsible reply. I then asked his surname. He said, "Kang." I was uncertain if that was his surname. I then left the Garrison Headquarters. Outside the gate, there was the Garrison Headquarters telephone. Two soldiers in gray cloth uniforms were sitting on the steps at the entrance. There was one officer of the Public Security Bureau Police Brigade with the number 4206, and one named Zhu from the Ordnance Factory Guard. According to the person named Zhu, besides the Police Brigade and the Guard, there were no other troops. I hereby submit the above report on the results of my observation to the Standing Board of Directors, Yang Youren.

The Railway Bureau Sent Police to the North Station Yesterday

To Guard Railway Property

Chen Xinghan, the director of both the Jin-Hu (Shanghai-Nanjing) and Hu-Hang-Yong (Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo) Railway Bureaus, due to a recent band of petty thieves who, taking advantage of the Japanese army not yet withdrawing from Zhenru and Zhabei, were secretly dismantling and selling railway property, specially went to the Reception Committee the day before yesterday and, together with a liaison officer from the committee, personally went to the Japanese consulate and the Japanese barracks to negotiate with Military Officer Harada and Major General Zhimatsu. Before the Japanese army withdraws, the Railway Bureau will send police to guard all railway property in advance. This was agreed to, and it was decided to first send twelve railway police officers to patrol around the North Station in shifts. Therefore, after 8:00 a.m. yesterday (the 19th), the twelve railway police officers guarding the railway property had entered the North Station.

The British Association Publicly

Advocates Convening a Round Table Conference 33

Foreigners Conspire to Plan Against Us

Ever since the idea of convening a round table conference emerged, the foreign community in Shanghai has been actively engaged, each eager to realize their long-held ambitions. The recent letter from the Shanghai British Association to various foreign chambers of commerce on the 14th provides a glimpse into their conspiracy. The translation of the letter is provided below, in the hope that our countrymen will make plans early and not regret their inaction later.

On the 13th of this month, the Board of Directors of our Association resolved: (1) To request your association to endorse the following resolution, which has been distributed to various foreign chambers of commerce in Shanghai. After obtaining unanimous endorsement, it will be forwarded to your government through the usual diplomatic channels. (2) To convene a special meeting of foreign taxpayers to propose the following resolution: "In view of the recent events in Shanghai, the Feetham Report, and in order to implement the resolution passed by the Council of the League of Nations on February 19th, the Shanghai Municipal Council is hereby instructed to urge the convening of an international conference to ensure the security of Shanghai, resolve the future status of Shanghai, and address other issues that frequently cause conflict and danger, with direct representation from the Shanghai Municipal Council attending the conference." Your association is hereby requested to endorse this resolution. Our Board of Directors also wishes to point out to you that unless concrete and effective action is taken at this time, all the problems that existed before January 28th will reappear in the future. These problems are: (1) the issue of extraterritorial roads; (2) Chinese armed forces around Shanghai; (3) the handling of litigation by the Special District Court. Regarding the first problem, your association is certainly aware from the newspapers that the Chinese have already strongly opposed the Municipal Council's road construction. These roads are all the property of the Municipal Council, as your association is well aware. Regarding the second problem, the stationing of unnecessary armed forces around Shanghai is extremely dangerous and could at any time lead to a repeat of the serious situation of 1927, necessitating the deployment of a large number of foreign troops to protect the concessions. Regarding the third issue, the Special District Court's improper handling of civil cases and lack of impartiality are obvious. Foreign merchants are well aware that even if they win a case, there is no agency to enforce it, so few seek relief from the court. This is also known to all foreigners. For these reasons, our Board of Directors believes that all foreign organizations should express their opinions to their governments, emphasizing the necessity of convening a round table conference, so that the world's major powers can resolve this and other issues. A copy of the resolution is attached. Please promptly endorse it, sign it, and return it. After all the foreign chambers of commerce have signed it, the resolution will be submitted for transmission to your government." The letter is signed by Huthai, Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Association.

Attached Resolution as Follows: 34

Whereas there are several incidents that affect the happiness and good government of Shanghai and are the cause of recent conflicts and disputes, especially the Special District Court, the right to manage extraterritorial roads, and the presence of armed troops in and around Shanghai, this Board of Directors believes that unless the aforementioned outstanding issues are resolved simultaneously, the recent Sino-Japanese dispute in Shanghai cannot be permanently and satisfactorily resolved. Therefore, the Board of Directors resolves that the consuls and diplomatic representatives of our country should apply for a round table conference to be convened as soon as possible by the major powers and China to resolve the outstanding issues affecting the happiness and good government of Shanghai. The Shanghai Municipal Council and the French Municipal Council may also send representatives to attend the conference.

(Note) The above resolution was read by the President of the Council of the League of Nations. It is claimed that the governments of the United States, Britain, and other relevant countries have endorsed the proposal. The full text is as follows: (1) A conference composed of representatives of the Chinese and Japanese governments, together with representatives of the other major powers mentioned above, should be organized immediately in Shanghai, with a view to bringing about a final end to the fighting and restoring peaceful conditions in Shanghai. (2) The basis of the conference should be: (a) on the part of Japan, the absence of any political or territorial designs and of any intention to establish a Japanese settlement in Shanghai or otherwise to advance the exclusive interests of the Japanese; (b) on the part of China, an undertaking to make effective provision for the maintenance of the safety and integrity of the International Settlement and the French Concession, and to prevent these areas and the people residing therein from being exposed to danger. (3) The meeting of the conference must, of course, be conditional on the conclusion of a local truce. The Council is confident that a truce can be arranged at an early date, and it suggests that the military, naval, and civil representatives of the other powers in Shanghai should give every assistance in bringing it about. (4) This proposal is designed to secure the immediate restoration of peace in the Shanghai area and does not prejudice or restrict the position of the League of Nations or any of the powers in regard to any of the issues raised by the Sino-Japanese dispute before the League.

According to the League of Nations overseas news released by the League of Nations Information Office, the Japanese government subsequently accepted this resolution. The Chinese government replied that, in accordance with the principles already announced, if a ceasefire is accepted and implemented, the Chinese government is prepared to participate in the Shanghai conference and acknowledges that the peace of the International Settlement and the French Concession is necessary for the maintenance of security in Shanghai and its surrounding areas. However, the conference is limited to restoring security in Shanghai, and all issues arising from the Sino-Japanese dispute in any part of China should be resolved in accordance with the procedures invoked by China at the League of Nations.

Japanese Soldiers in Wusong Shoot and Kill a Chinese 35

Xu Xiangzhu, a victim of the language barrier

Xu Xiangsheng, a resident of Wenchang Road in Wusong, was walking alone to the corner of Hefeng Road at about 8:30 the night before last when he was suddenly stopped and inspected by Japanese patrol military police in the darkness. Because Xu could not understand the language, he turned around and ran away. The Japanese soldier immediately fired a shot, which struck Xu in a vital spot, causing him to fall to the ground and die. Xu's mother rushed to the scene upon hearing the news and wept over his body. However, Wusong is still under the trampling of iron hooves, and there is no way to appeal for justice. Yesterday, they could only hastily arrange for his burial.

Japanese Troops Withdraw Sequentially 36

The various units of the 35th Regiment of the 17th Brigade Infantry of the Japanese 9th Division, stationed in the Jiangwan area, have already withdrawn yesterday and concentrated in Wusong and Yangshupu, preparing to depart for home. A squad of military police also left Shanghai at the same time. Since yesterday, military supplies and ammunition have been transported to the docks. The Army Ministry has also sent the transport ships Nōwei Maru and Kōchi Maru to Shanghai, berthed at Wusong and Dalian Wharf, scheduled to carry the troops back to Japan tomorrow. The Japanese troops withdrawing from Jiangwan, the various infantry and artillery units that have moved to the east of the railway, are scheduled to hold a drill at the Jiangwan Stadium at 9:00 a.m. today, stipulating that the infantry and cavalry units practice the military actions of attacking and raiding. These Japanese troops are also scheduled to leave Shanghai on the 21st. Previously, because many naval and army personnel were traveling between Japan and Shanghai, the Japanese Metropolitan Police Department specially formed a ticket inspection committee to exclusively check the tickets of the soldiers traveling by ship, in order to calculate the discount and payment with the shipping companies. Now, because all the Japanese troops are withdrawing, there is no need to retain this ticket inspection work, and it is being terminated. After remaining for another ten days, it will be abolished.

Ma Zhanshan's Troops Repeatedly Defeat Japanese Forces 37

Self-Defense Army only five li from Harbin. The Songpu Power Plant was destroyed by artillery fire. Overseas Chinese donated aircraft also participated in the war. Longjiang Arsenal moved to Heihe. It is said that Ma's troops are well-equipped and disciplined, and are supported by local militias and volunteer forces, with numbers steadily increasing. (Reuter, 19th)

(Harbin) The anti-Manchukuo army is fiercely attacking Harbin, five miles from the city, but has failed to advance and is now retreating. The Songpu (transliteration) power plant near Harbin was destroyed by artillery fire from the anti-Manchukuo army, but the damage is not significant. Warehouses and houses along the Huhuai Line have also been largely destroyed by bombing. It is reported that many civilians have been killed or injured, but the exact number is unknown. (Reuter, 19th)

Guangdong Air Force Two Captains

Telegraphic Opposition to Reorganization 59

Liu Zhiyan and Zhou Bocheng Decide to Resign

(Hong Kong) Liu Zhiyan and Zhou Bocheng of the Guangdong Air Force sent a telegraph on the 18th, addressed to all newspaper offices and organizations for their public assessment: "The Air Force is a national defense force. This sudden merger by the First Army Group of Guangdong is, in reason and law, right or wrong. It is obvious to all and requires no further elaboration. However, Chen Jitang telegraphed to Beijing, claiming that the Air Force internally 'urgently requests to be taken back for reorganization,' and that if it is not taken back, they will resign en masse and go elsewhere. Matters of personal integrity make it impossible to remain silent. Looking back, our Air Force has gone through the sacrifices of countless martyrs, and the guidance of Commander-in-Chief Zhang for more than ten years, establishing a glorious history. Through difficult management, it has been able to stand alone, transforming personal military force into the force of the people, with the principle of not participating in civil wars. Therefore, resisting Japan and suppressing the Communists have proceeded in separate ways. In total, our Air Force has five squadrons. At the beginning of the Shanghai battle, Squadron Leader Ding Ji-xu of our Second Squadron led his planes north. Recently, when the Communist bandits invaded Guangdong, Zhiyan led the Fifth Squadron to Shantou, and Bocheng led the Third Squadron to Shaozhou, all to suppress the Communists. Furthermore, Commander Hu Jin-ya of our Second Group went far to America. The incident occurred suddenly, and Zhiyan and Bocheng's squadrons were not informed beforehand and were monitored afterward. The so-called 'urgent request to be taken back for reorganization' must be that one or two people blinded by profit are willing to once again turn the people's military force into a personal military force, to fulfill their private ambitions of seizing power. This not only betrays the enthusiasm of the people who have supported the Air Force for months but also destroys the glorious history of our Air Force for more than ten years. Zhiyan and others have their own principles of conduct, and they are determined to leave, firm in their conviction. Now, as private citizens, we do not wish to comment too much, but the facts are there, and righteousness resides in the masses. At this time of national crisis, they are still seizing power and grasping for personal gain. How can they face the people of our country? We must sincerely and openly express our feelings. Since things have come to this, what more can be said? Our original intention of resisting Japan and suppressing the Communists has not been forgotten for a single day. We dare to make this statement, hoping for your understanding and consideration. Liu Zhiyan, Zhou Bocheng, and others respectfully salute." (19th Special Telegram)

Japanese Ambassador Arima

Eight National Railway Workers' Unions

Yesterday's Joint Meeting 62

Eleven Resolutions

Telegram to the Investigation Team Opposing the Northeast Puppet Organization

(Tianjin) Eight national railway workers' unions held a joint meeting on the 19th, and the resolutions are as follows: (1) Telegram to the League of Nations Investigation Team opposing the Northeast puppet organization. (2) The Beining Railway Workers' Union is responsible for investigating unemployed workers and casualties in the Northeast, reporting to the Central Government and forwarding to the Ministry of Railways for condolences and preferential employment. (3) Telegram to the Central Government requesting the speedy recovery of lost territory in the Northeast by force. (4) During the national crisis, each railway workers' union should cooperate with the railway administration to supervise and lead the employees of each railway to work hard, increase production, and increase income. (5) Telegram to the Central Government requesting the Ministry of Railways to order all railway administrations to stop transporting Japanese goods and to order all railway workers not to purchase Japanese goods. (6) Petition to the Central Government to provide relief to disaster victims in the war zones and Communist bandit areas. (7) Petition to the Central Government to transfer to the Ministry of Railways to send personnel to each railway to cooperate with the union to investigate and dismiss redundant personnel and to determine the number of staff members according to the business conditions of each railway to avoid abuse. (8) If any railway workers' union finds a private sale of railway cars, it will report to the Central Government for strict handling. (9) Appeal to the Central Government during the national crisis to strictly order civil and military officials throughout the country to work hard to save the country. (10) Appeal to the Central Government to transfer to the Ministry of Railways to pay close attention to the purchase of materials on each railway to avoid malpractices. (11) Appeal to the Central Government to transfer to the Ministry of Railways to unify the treatment of workers and staff on national railways. In addition, the joint transportation tickets received by employees and family members serving in national railways should be free of charge. The telegram to the League of Nations is as follows: "Nanjing International Labor Organization China Branch transfers to the Geneva League of Nations Secretariat and the Northeast League of Nations Investigation Team for public review. The Japanese Empire violated the League of Nations Covenant and the Nine-Power Treaty, and at the expense of destroying world peace, suddenly occupied our Northeast with troops on September 18, 1931, expelled our officials, violated our sovereignty, and killed our compatriots, disregarding the resolutions of the League of Nations. It has created a Northeast puppet organization to deceive the world and attempt to fulfill its aggressive ambitions. The Chinese nation can never recognize it. Looking at the resistance to the puppet organization everywhere in the Northeast, it has no popular support and no autonomy. It is only the Japanese Empire that uses force to support the situation and calls it a country. Who can believe it? Moreover, the Northeast is our territory, and Japan has forcibly occupied it by force. This association is determined to lead the railway workers of the whole country as the government's backing, deny all puppet organizations in the Northeast, and hope to uphold justice, clarify justice, and promptly withdraw Japanese troops and return our Northeast to maintain peace. Fortunately in East Asia, fortunately in the world. The joint conference of the National Railway Workers' Unions of the Republic of China bows." (19th Special Telegram)

Scope of the Amnesty Case 76

Majority Opinion of the Legislative Yuan

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan has discussed the amnesty case more than a dozen times. The majority opinion is that corrupt officials and Communist Party members should not be generally pardoned. For military offenders, it seems appropriate to use military regulations, but the National Government promulgated the Army, Navy, and Air Force Criminal Law only half a year ago. Foreign News

Soviet Russia is Eagerly Preparing for Military Expansion 117

Five Million Reserve Soldiers Mobilized for Exercises Nationwide Aviation Personnel Ordered to Participate Berlin Closely Watching the Development of the Far East Situation

Moscow, 18th National News Agency, Today's announcement here is that Soviet Russia will hold a major exercise for the Red Guards and local security forces. The government has telegraphed all members of the National Popular Aviation Association to prepare to report to various airfields on the specified date so that all aviators can participate in the exercises. The purpose of the Popular Aviation Association is to democratize aviation and air defense, with 8 million members. Its most important function is to train junior aviators who have just passed the aviation test so that they can pursue further studies.

Berlin, 19th National News Agency, Today's Forward Newspaper of the German Social Democratic Party stated that the Far East situation is showing increasingly tense signs. According to the radio news released by the Soviet Russian authorities in Berlin, Stalin originally planned to go to the Crimean resorts to enjoy the long summer, but he suddenly decided to cancel it because he expected a sudden development of the situation. Also, the People's Commissar of the Army, Voroshilov, was scheduled to speak on the radio last night, but the Moscow radio station suddenly announced temporarily that Voroshilov had been summoned to an important meeting and canceled the speech. In addition, there is an important sign of tense situation. The Moscow Supreme Military Commission has decided to convene reserve servicemen of the 1909, 1910, 1911, and 1912 grades to participate in this year's major exercises or join local security forces or join the Red Guards, and no excuses are allowed. The newspaper believes that the aforementioned news can cause great fear, and the decision to mobilize reserve soldiers will cause 4 to 5 million people to arm and drill, which can be called a terrible military demonstration. It is still remembered that on May 1, the Moscow Labor Day parade had 100,000 defense troops with the latest weapons marching through Red Square, plus 300 aircraft circling the sky. If compared with this, it can also be seen that the Russians are eagerly preparing for military expansion.

Berlin, 19th Reuters, Germany is deeply aware of the potential crisis in the current situation in the Far East, so it is closely watching its development. People from all walks of life are afraid that after the military controls Japanese policy, it will eventually lead to a conflict between China and Russia against Japan, which will affect the world. Everyone agrees that if the Japanese government succumbs to the demands of the military and intends to occupy Manchuria, it will inevitably lead to armed resistance from China and Russia. The general opinion is that Soviet Russia has exhausted political and diplomatic methods to contain this war. Although the German political circles are also afraid that the current situation will result in international disputes, they still hope that Japanese peacemakers can prevent the military's fanatics from engaging in adventures with unpredictable consequences.

Japanese Military Power Controls Policy

Suzuki Cabinet Formation Faces Many Obstacles 118

Military Firmly Opposes a Political Party Cabinet

Araki and Suzuki Still Find Their Opinions Difficult to Reconcile

Dentsu, 19th, Tokyo Dispatch: Regarding the successor to the Suzuki cabinet, a person was again dispatched this morning to negotiate with the military. The military consistently insists on realizing a national unity cabinet and opposes a political party cabinet. Therefore, even if the imperial mandate descends upon Suzuki, Suzuki will inevitably encounter obstacles when forming the cabinet.

Reuters, 19th, Tokyo Dispatch: According to well-informed sources, the claim that Araki and Suzuki have reached an understanding is premature. It is said that the military is still strongly advocating a large-scale elimination of the evils of political parties and the relief of farmers and small business owners. However, Suzuki is unwilling to undertake such far-reaching reforms immediately. Therefore, the point of contention seems extremely important. The military traditionally detests the bourgeoisie. Its soldiers are recruited from rural areas and naturally sympathize with impoverished farmers. They feel that farmers are burdened by heavy taxes, while the giants of industry and commerce profit from them. Therefore, they believe that to avoid further deterioration, the evils of the Japanese party system must be eradicated, and the living conditions of farmers must be improved. Politicians and the military have different positions. Their power largely depends on the political party spoils system, which is closely related to the financial cliques. Therefore, they cannot undertake excessive reforms.

Far East News Agency, 19th, Tokyo Dispatch: The Japanese cabinet formation problem still faces many twists and turns. After Suzuki met with Araki at 4 p.m. yesterday, the general public believed that the opinions of the Seiyukai and the Army Ministry had become consistent. However, based on the current situation, not only have Suzuki and Araki not reached a consensus, but their opinions are also trending towards opposition. Therefore, the cabinet formation issue will be difficult to decide today or tomorrow. Suzuki sent Morikaku, the Secretary-General of the Seiyukai, to run errands and mediate with Araki several times today, but to no avail. After Suzuki met with Araki yesterday, it was widely rumored that the opinions of the two factions had become consistent, which surprised the military. Chief of Staff Mazaki personally inquired with Araki today about the fact that he had compromised with the Suzuki faction, but Araki absolutely denied it and explained that yesterday's meeting with Suzuki was merely a social courtesy. The fundamental issues regarding the cabinet formation and the position taken by the Army Ministry have not yet been resolved.

Hua Lian News Agency, 19th, Tokyo Dispatch: It is said that young Japanese army officers are extremely indignant that Minister of the Army Araki will compromise with Prime Minister Suzuki and have begun a movement against a political party cabinet. Upon hearing the news, veterans in various regions are extremely excited and have sent representatives to the capital to cooperate with the young officers. Youth groups have also sent representatives to the capital to join the fascist movement, and the momentum is very strong.

Summons a Meeting of Senior Statesmen

A Strange Young Man Submits a Petition

Suzuki first stated the Emperor's intentions and then held talks on the political situation for thirty minutes. Therefore, Saionji's recommendation for a successor cabinet is highly regarded by all parties. However, the military's attitude is strong, and a portion of the government is still advocating for a Hiranuma cabinet. Cecil Expresses

Disarmament Conference is Hopeless 126

The purpose of this conference is not war, nor is it to discuss how to defeat the enemy, but to reduce the danger of war. How can those whose profession is warfare negotiate?

Osaka Mainichi Shimbun Argues 133

A Japanese-American War is Imminent

(Continued)

Since the outbreak of the Manchurian Incident, the relationship between Japan and the United States has been an unfortunate breeding ground for crises. Now, they are concentrating their entire fleet on the Pacific Ocean and holding large-scale exercises centered on Honolulu, which is clear evidence of their ambition. However, we recall the unreasonable and coercive diplomatic means of the past, the so-called "domination of the vast world." For a specific country, to achieve its own ambition or imply its own hostility, it does not hesitate to lightly mobilize the entire army and navy to threaten the opposing country. In European diplomatic history, the two countries of Germany and Russia, which clearly advocated militarism, moved from the era of power and deceit to the era of the outbreak of war. Compared to the United Kingdom and France, which received free air, why did disputes arise in their relations? Because the opposing country always faced them with swords and guns. In September 1910, the German Emperor visited the Vienna City Hall and repeatedly threatened Russia with the annexation of Bosnia. At that time, Europe was greatly affected by the unreasonable demands and verbal threats of diplomacy and felt uneasy.

Although the current U.S. government is not following in the footsteps of Europe, President Roosevelt led a fleet to pressure Yokohama two years before the German Emperor's visit to Vienna, threatening Japan with a demonstration of force and etiquette. Since the Great War in Europe, the international concepts of the past have disappeared. President Wilson, as a leader of peace, advocated disarmament and the elimination of war. Unexpectedly, today the United States is contradicting its purpose, adopting the unreasonable and coercive diplomatic creed again, and mobilizing its entire fleet for no reason, provoking the warlike desires of the people of both Japan and the United States. Its rash actions are truly puzzling to us. Generally, a great country with dignity should maintain its attitude as a great country. The large-scale exercise in Honolulu is nothing less than performing an uneasy and challenging behavior in front of the Japanese people's door. Its transgressions are self-evident. Now, the U.S. Navy insists on holding exercises in Honolulu, the center of the Pacific. What is the meaning of this? Judging from the current Japan-U.S. relations, we can already be fearful. What is particularly concerning is that the actions of the U.S. Navy in the future may exceed the norm. The reconnaissance fleet, which should have returned to the Atlantic after the large-scale exercise, suddenly changed its scheduled plan and stayed in the Pacific indefinitely. Judging from the surrounding situation, it can be further proven that the U.S. government's intention is to prepare for war in the Pacific step by step. At this crisis, if either the individual or the whole loses its self-control slightly, it can lead to an irreparable crisis. The large-scale exercise they are holding in Honolulu is already offending us. If their reconnaissance fleet remains in the Pacific permanently, if they are not careful, endless storms will inevitably occur. This is why I am worried about the future of Japan and the United States. (To be continued)

Important News Two

Employees of the Chinese Eastern Railway 134

Russia Replenishes with Soldiers

Intended to Facilitate Military Operations

Nagasaki Nichinichi Shimbun reported that recently, a large number of Russian employees on the entire Chinese Eastern Railway have been laid off and replaced with active-duty and reserve soldiers. Russia is secretly replenishing vacancies, fearing that in the event of a major incident, they can immediately concentrate at predetermined locations and participate in military operations. They plan to concentrate employees from the western line between Anda and Zhanzishan in Angangxi to guard the Taoang Road. Weapons and ammunition are fully prepared.

Japanese Military Circles Discuss Unifying 135

Manchurian Four-Headed Politics

A Marshal Governor-General Will Be Established

Nagasaki Nichinichi Shimbun reported that the Manchurian-Mongolian Committee, organized by the chiefs of the General Staff and the Army Ministry, has decided to appoint the Commander of the Kwantung Army, General Oshima, as the Governor-General of Kwantung to unify the four-headed politics of Manchuria. The consuls and consuls are placed under the Governor-General of Kwantung. The relationship between the Kwantung Government and Manchuria and Mongolia will remain the same as the current system, that is, the army and navy will be the center, and a unified plan will be established. This system will be submitted to the Cabinet Council. However, this bill is only a provisional system during the period before the recognition of Manchukuo. After the official recognition is realized, it will be expanded and revised from the root, and a marshal-level governor-general will be established.

General Japanese Public Opinion 136

Opposes Dictatorship

Supports the Constitutional System

World News Translation Agency Tokyo Yomiuri Shimbun reported that a political conspiracy, the likes of which the empire has never seen in its history, is threatening the foundation of the empire. Among the many reactionary movements, the most prominent is the fascist movement, which is advocated by Privy Council Vice President Hiranuma and seems to be gaining the sympathy and support of the people. Hiranuma recently stated that the reactionary movement initiated by his political group, the Kokuhonsha, is completely different from Italian fascism. However, we cannot see where the differences lie. Hiranuma's party opposes constitutional convention and all other political parties, and advocates the establishment of a dictatorship to control all state organs. A large portion of public opinion is surprisingly supportive of this dangerous movement. There is no doubt that the rise of reactionary tendencies and their widespread sympathy are due to the incompetence of existing political parties and the selfishness of politicians. Political parties and their leaders disregard the happiness of the country and the people, causing the people to gradually increase their resentment towards them. The failure of the political parties has naturally caused reactionary movements. I fear that the time remaining for the political parties to fight for their lives is running out. We support those who sincerely uphold constitutionalism on the one hand and do not hesitate to warn the leaders of the political parties to quickly change their ways so that the people's trust in the political parties may still be retained.

Moreover, Miyako Shimbun said that the Minseito issued a statement denouncing fascism and all reactionary political tendencies. We feel that the Minseito and most of the public recognize that the so-called fascism that is rising in the empire is a doctrine that absolutely denies parliamentary politics. Italian fascism does not advocate violence. Although it has gained the support of the entire nation, the parliamentary system is still maintained. Therefore, it is a mistake to recognize fascism as conflicting with constitutionalism. The Japanese constitution was established since the Meiji Emperor's Restoration and is determined to be the permanent political system of the empire. Anyone who openly doubts or attempts to overthrow this foundation of the country, whether left-leaning or right-leaning, should of course be subject to strict legal sanctions. It is noteworthy that a certain group of soldiers absolutely deny the existence and powers of the Imperial Diet and, at the same time, disregard the restrictions imposed on the army and navy by the Imperial Constitution. This is truly strange.

The Warlord Bandits Withdraw from Zhengyang 138

Due to attacks by the local militia and Red Spear Society

The bandits retreated towards Yingheji

The local aftermath urgently needs to be addressed

Bengbu Correspondence: After the bandits occupied Zhengyang, they looted wantonly for several days, kidnapping men and women and looting property, filling more than forty boats in total, and sailing upstream. The bandits entrenched inside and outside the town wantonly destroyed, causing the local area to be devastated. Cheng Yi's unit, the 718th Regiment of the 40th Independent Brigade of the Army, and Wang Shaojiu's unit, the 719th Regiment, were dispatched from Huoqiu to encircle and suppress them. When the troops reached Yuezhangji in Fengtai County, they adopted an encirclement strategy, attacking Zhengyang step by step. They came into contact with the bandits near Zhengyang a few days ago, and the battle was fierce, killing many bandits. Five or sixty soldiers of the Wang Regiment were killed or wounded, and the Cheng Regiment also suffered some casualties. Yang Chengxuan, the leader of the militia in Shouxian, Fengtai, and Ying Shang counties (from Yang Naozi, west of Zhengyang), also gathered thousands of local militia and Red Spear Society martial arts teams, uniting to attack the bandits. Seeing that the militia's guns and equipment were sophisticated and the momentum was huge, the bandits knew it would be difficult to resist, so at 5:00 AM on the 15th, they abandoned Zhengyang and retreated towards Mengjiawan and Yingheji. Before leaving, they took many more hostages. After this catastrophe in Zhengyang, the local essence has been completely lost. It will be difficult to recover within three to five years. After the headquarters of the Second Garrison Brigade here received definite news that the bandits had withdrawn from Zhengyang, Brigade Commander Li Yanqing immediately ordered Ni, the regimental commander stationed in Fengtai, to lead the first and second battalions of his regiment and various companies and platoons of machine guns, mortars, and communications to advance to Zhengyang and suppress the bandits as the opportunity arose. Song Shike, the brigade commander of the 40th Independent Brigade, arrived in Bengbu from Nanjing and, yesterday (the 15th) at 11:00 AM, also took a plane to scout around Zhengyang. Two planes went with him and dropped two bombs, both of which exploded upon landing, but the bandits had already withdrawn in the morning. It is unknown whether any innocent civilians were injured. Song Shike flew back in the afternoon. Today (the 16th) at 10:00 AM, he led his guards on the Jiangning ship from Bengbu to Zhengyang to supervise the suppression of the bandits. The Chamber of Commerce here received a telegram from the Shouxian Chamber of Commerce this morning (the 16th), also stating that the bandits had left Zhengyang and fled to the southeast, closer to Shou County, requesting that Wang's Brigade (i.e., the 10th Brigade of Xu Tingyao's 4th Division) be quickly requested to come to Shou to defend and suppress them. I just met with Yu Yumen, the head of the Zhengyang Defense Corps. According to him, the bandits did retreat to Mengjiawan, southwest of Zhengyang. Zhengyang has been devastated by this banditry. However, Mengjiawan is only twelve li away from Zhengyang. Although the bandits have temporarily retreated, optimism is not warranted. It is hoped that the Central Army will quickly pursue and suppress the bandits from Bengbu to save the survivors. Furthermore, handling the local aftermath brooks no delay. (16th)

Han Fuqu's Exhortation 139

Officers and soldiers protect the country and defend the people

Gathered officers for a joint celebration

Reviewed troops stationed in Jinan

Jinan Correspondence: Han Fuqu, Commander-in-Chief of the Third Route Army, is now taking the opportunity to summon division and brigade commanders to Jinan in stages for joint celebrations, as banditry throughout the province has been largely suppressed and the region is gradually becoming stable. They will also discuss local defense matters together. He held a banquet for brigade commanders and militia commanders on the 15th and held a grand review on the 16th. The situation is described as follows:

The Provincial Government's Banquet: At 9:00 AM on the 15th, division and brigade commanders and militia commanders gathered in the East Building of the Provincial Government. Those present included Division Commanders Sun Tongxuan, Gu Liangmin, and Qiao Lizhi; Headquarters Chief of Staff Liu Shuxiang; Building Director Zhang Shaotang; Military Law Department Director Li Wuchen; Quartermaster Department Director Tian Lianzhong; Military Affairs Department Director Xie Huawen; Ordnance Department Director Liu Kewen; Public Relations Department Director Zhang Xiyao; Medical Department Director Wang Qingxi; Wireless Management Office Director Zhang Yunting; Aide-de-Camp Han Wenxiu; Armored Car Commander Dai Hongbin; He Mengjiu, representative of Deputy Commander Liu Guitang of the Shandong Garrison; Second Route Commander Guo Wensheng; Brigade Commanders Lei Taiping, Li Hanzhang, Li Yizhi, Tang Bangzhi, Yun Qichang, Ning Chunxiao, Rong Guangxing, Ma Guanyi, Ma Jingong, Zhang Shulin, Li Zhanbiao, Chen Dexin, Zhao Xinde; Lunan Militia Commander Xie Shuxian; Luxi Militia Commander Gu Liangyou; Ludong Militia Commander Zhao Mingyuan; and Lubei Militia Commander Zhao Renquan, totaling more than thirty people. After all the participants arrived, Han Fuqu reported the significance of this gathering and the current situation, including domestic military and diplomatic affairs. He stated that he had not seen everyone for a long time, and it was rare for everyone stationed in the outer defenses to come to Jinan at the same time and gather together. The overall situation is currently relatively peaceful, the Shanghai war has been resolved, and the Japanese army is gradually withdrawing. Our country is preparing to take over the occupied areas. The Guangdong incident was purely a misunderstanding and has been mediated without incident. As for the military and political aspects of this province, it can be said that they have entered the right track. Bandits in various places have been gradually suppressed, and local security is gradually becoming stable. Brigade commanders and militia commanders are mostly stationed in outer counties and are close to the people. It is hoped that they will understand the hardships of the people, earnestly suppress bandits, protect the region, and fulfill the military's duty to protect the country and defend the people. Rewards and punishments for subordinates must be clear and fair, and there must be no incidents of disturbing the people. The significance of gathering everyone in Jinan is, first, to meet each other and get together to talk freely; second, if everyone has ideas or things that should be developed or reformed in terms of defense, they can be brought up for joint discussion to facilitate rectification. Around 10:00 AM, after the speech, they went to the West Flower Hall for a meal, and dispersed after 11:00 AM.

The Grand Review at Xinzhuang: In the morning of the 16th, Han ordered the troops stationed in Jinan to gather at Xinzhuang for a review. In addition to Han Fuqu, those present at the review included Division Commanders Sun Tongxuan and Qiao Lizhi; Brigade Commanders Lei Taiping, Tang Bangzhi, Yun Qichang, Chen Dexin, Li Hanzhang, Rong Guangxing, Li Yizhi, Ma Jingong, Zhang Shulin, Li Zhanbiao, Zhao Xinde, Ning Chunxiao, Ma Guanyi; He Mengjiu, representative of Deputy Commander Liu Guitang of the Shandong Garrison; Second Route Commander Guo Tiansheng; Armored Car Commander Dai Hongbin; Headquarters Chief of Staff Liu Shuxiang; and various department heads. In addition to the Third Route Army troops stationed in Jinan, the 26th Route Army Heavy Artillery Battalion was also included, totaling the General Headquarters Guard Company, Pistol Brigade, Special Service Battalion, the 20th Division Headquarters and Special Service Battalion, the entire 58th Brigade, the entire 60th Brigade, the 74th Division Headquarters and Special Service Battalion, the entire 220th Brigade, the Engineering Battalion, Communications Battalion, and Railway Artillery Unit stationed in Jinan, various unit companies, various mortar companies and battalions, the 20th Division Artillery Regiment, the 26th Route Army Heavy Artillery Battalion, and various cavalry companies, totaling more than 20,000 people. All the troops receiving the review arrived at the Xinzhuang parade ground before 7:00 AM to await inspection. The review commander was Sun Tongxuan, the commander of the 20th Division. After the troops were arranged in order, the review began at 8:00 AM. The reviewing officers rode around for a week to inspect. After the review, Han delivered a speech, stating that because the brigade commanders were stationed throughout Shandong Province, some counties were far from the province, and defense was important, it was not easy to see each other. Only a quarter of the troops were stationed in the province, and three-quarters were outside the province. Therefore, he took the opportunity of the brigade commanders coming to the province to see each other, and this was the meaning of today's gathering and review. We were born in the Republic of China, and are part of the people of the Republic of China, and also part of the military. What to do and what responsibilities to bear, everyone has been in the army for many years, and there is no need to say more. We are passing through day by day, month by month, year by year, and we must pay attention to time, and also make knowledge and thinking move forward with time. Doing more things while passing more time is not a wasted life. As an ordinary person, it is inevitable that one does not fully understand the situation of national diplomacy and internal affairs, but as a soldier and a civil servant, one must be clear about the national situation. In terms of the current international situation, in short, it is nothing more than Japan's invasion of China. The detailed situation is recorded in the newspapers, and everyone has probably seen it. People in the country are too disappointing, and everyone does not work hard, which has caused international troubles. Everyone knows my personality after being together for many years, so there is no need to talk about domestic and foreign situations. What everyone needs to pay attention to is understanding their responsibilities. Living in a certain place, one must fulfill the responsibilities of a soldier in that place. When foreigners invade, one must fulfill the responsibility of protecting territory, protecting sovereignty, and protecting the people. One must die at the right place and at the right time. Life and death are nothing, but they must have value. Domestically, one must protect the people's safety, and treat the people with kindness and patience, because most of the rural people have not received education, but soldiers, no matter what, have received education. For the people, even if one suffers a little loss, it is only right. Especially, everyone must understand that since ancient times, only those who can become one with the people can stand firm. Even if they fail, they will gain sympathy from public opinion. Although defeated, what is the difference from success? In the past, King Wu of Zhou had very few people, but he defeated tens of thousands of people. During the Three Kingdoms period, Yuan Shao and the Yellow Turbans had many people, but they ultimately failed. History proves that success or failure depends entirely on whether or not one gains the hearts of the people. It only depends on discipline. Good military discipline can win the sympathy of the people, and then one can win more with less. It is not only relying on skillful command and careful planning, but the main reason lies in the people. Yue Fei of the Song Dynasty was good at defeating more with less and greatly defeated the Jin people. The soldiers he led would rather starve to death than steal food from the people, and would rather freeze to death than enter civilian houses, protecting the people everywhere, so he ultimately gained the people's admiration. The key lies in harmony, not in numbers. It is impossible not to unite with the people. I hope everyone will use their brains more on this. Furthermore, in training the troops, there are different methods for winter, spring, and autumn. In spring and autumn, there can be more field exercises. In summer, when the weather is too hot, pay more attention to mental lectures and individual training to make them understand the situation of national humiliation and plan for the people, with a spirit of sacrifice. Often conduct guerrilla training in the woods. Furthermore, special attention must be paid to the training of newly recruited soldiers. New soldiers are like new brides. They are free at home, but after marriage, everything is restricted. When new soldiers come to the barracks, all aspects of life change. They must be treated with sympathy and trained slowly. Do not seek too much too quickly, and then there will be good results. After Han finished speaking, the officers returned to their respective teams. Han then spoke with the brigade commanders until 11:00 AM before dispersing. (16th)

Central Government Takes Back 140

Shandong National Tax Agencies

Han's troops' military pay is still allocated monthly by the Central Government

Jinan Correspondence: Han Fuqu of the Shandong Third Route Army recently borrowed Central Government tax funds to maintain the soldiers' livelihood due to the lack of military pay. He appointed people to act as agents in the national tax agencies in Shandong, such as the Salt Transport Envoy, the Luyu Regional Unified Tax Bureau, the Jinan Branch, the Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau, the Lu Da Mining Tax Office, the Zhongxing Mining Tax Office, and the Smoke Tax Bureau, except for Ren Wenhan, the Director of the Nitrates and Minerals Bureau. This has been going on for several months. Recently, Jiang Bocheng, representative of the Central Government, came to Jinan to meet with Han and negotiate a solution to restore the original state of the national tax system so that the Central Government's authority can be unified. Han stated that as long as the Central Government distributes military pay, the soldiers can maintain their livelihood, and the national tax agencies can be returned. Therefore, Jiang and Han proceeded to study the method of returning them. Except for the Salt Transport Envoy, where the Central Government appointed Li Fengyao, and the Binnan Branch of the Luyu Unified Tax Bureau, where the Central Government appointed Xu Tierui, the rest were recommended by Han. It is rumored that Li Wuchen, Director of the Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau, Meng Zhaokong, Deputy Director, and Li Rukui of the Lu Da Mining Tax Office (details of the Zhongxing Mining Tax Office and the Smoke Tax Bureau are unknown) were all appointed by the Central Government. Han's troops' monthly military pay is still 600,000 yuan, which will be issued by the Central Government in the future. Han expressed satisfaction with this. Jiang then hosted a banquet for the new and old Salt Transport Envoys and the new and old Jinan Directors of the Unified Tax Bureau to discuss the handover methods. It is rumored that it was decided to hand over on the 18th. Jiang Bocheng left Jinan for Beiping tonight (the 16th) after his official duties were completed. According to Jiang's remarks when he left Jinan, "The Shandong national tax agencies have all been returned to the Central Government. All personnel will be appointed by the Central Government. Han's troops' military pay will be issued by the Central Government on time in the future. The result is satisfactory, and there should be no more rumors from the outside world. As for the current salt tax surcharges, the Ministry of Finance will issue an order to handle them. Since my affairs have been completed, I will return to Beiping tonight." Xu Tieshan also said that the Jinan Collection Office of the Luyu Unified Tax Bureau will be taken over on the 18th. The revenue situation of the Shandong unified tax is estimated to be more than 40,000 yuan per month for wheat flour tax, more than 30,000 yuan for match tax, and more than 20,000 yuan for cotton yarn tax. Plans will be made to organize them in the future, and there should be further increases. (16th)

Guangdong Province 141

Full of internal war scenes

Deng Longguang takes over the Navy Department

Inland river ships are stationed in sections

Forts are being built near Guangzhou

Guangzhou Correspondence: Chen Jitang's capture of part of Chen Ce's fleet has led to a situation where part of the air force (Zhang Huichang's faction) is concentrated in Qiongya with the outgoing fleet, forming a confrontational situation with Chen Jitang's army. Recently, Chen Jitang has been particularly anxious to deal with the air force and navy in Qiongya. On the 11th, he sent Chief Counselor Deng Longguang to take over the Navy Headquarters. At 9:00 AM that day, Deng arrived at the Navy Headquarters to take over all files, documents, and public property, and summoned the captains of the inland river ships who had surrendered to the headquarters to give them instructions. He encouraged the captains and then called the roll of the captains and reappointed them. They included Huang Zhaotang, captain of the Jianru ship; Yao Dong, captain of the Zhongkai ship; He Yilu, captain of the Zhongyuan ship; Du Chunxin, captain of the Haifang ship; Wen Hangang, captain of the Guang'an ship; Tang Zhenxing, captain of the Zhongzheng ship; Chen Mingchuan, captain of the Cunjin ship; Wu Zili, captain of the Fuyou ship; Zhang Cheng, captain of the Anxin ship; Gu Shengkai, captain of the Jiangshun ship; He Dong, captain of the Jinma ship; Cen Tanzhi, captain of the Guangdong ship; Li Yuanchu, captain of the Yuexing ship; and Zhou Changqi, captain of the Guanghua ship; Tan Xiangrong, captain of the Lichen ship. In addition to the naval headquarters staff, those who resigned were replaced, and the rest temporarily continued to work as usual. After Deng took over the Navy Headquarters, he also announced to all parties that he was acting as the Navy Commander and would no longer hold an inauguration ceremony. On the same day, Chen Jitang also appointed Li Qingwen as Deputy Navy Commander and Li Julu as Chief of Staff of the Navy Headquarters. As for Zhao Guizhang, who took over the fleet a few days ago, he is currently responsible for unblocking the return of the captains to the team and will not take office for the time being, only serving as the captain of the Guangjin ship. However, Zhao went to meet with Chen Ce in and went to Macau to contact the captains of the outgoing ships, but it is said that he has not gained anything and has returned to the province to report everything to Chen Jitang. Chen Jitang, seeing that Chen Ce's outgoing fleet was entrenched in Hainan (i.e., Qiongya), made strict precautions in advance. The inland river ships that have surrendered have recently been ordered to be stationed in sections in various inland rivers, paying particular attention to the defense of the West River in order to prevent Chen Ce's outgoing ships from attacking. Forts have also been built at Changjianggang and Xiuyinggang, strategically important locations in Dashan Township near Guangzhou. Trenches have been dug around the forts, and the mountain artillery team directly under the Second Army is stationed there permanently. Two 7.5-inch heavy cannons, several anti-aircraft guns, and more than ten mortars are installed on the forts to control the air and sea raids on Guangzhou. At the same time, ships entering and leaving the river surface of the fort are inspected. Ships without a pass from the First Group Army Headquarters are not allowed to pass. Therefore, the fort's defense is no less than that of the Humen and Changzhou forts. Since Chen Jitang's defense of Guangzhou is so strict, he will further send troops to attack Qiongya during the day. It is rumored that Chen Zhangfu, a member of the South District Pacification Department, will be appointed as the Commander for Bandit Suppression in Qiongya. Chen has been summoned back to the province and will return to the South Road to make arrangements after Chen Jitang's instructions. Chen Jitang also plans to transfer four to five regiments of troops from Xiang Hanping's unit of the Second Army to the South Road to be commanded by Chen Zhangfu to attack Qiongya. Therefore, the local civil war in Guangdong Province will begin immediately. (May 13th)

Local News

National Crisis Relief Association 146

Denounces the Ceasefire Agreement

The National Crisis Relief Association telegraphed: "To all newspaper offices and the people of the Korean National Convention, the Shanghai Feng War Agreement was hastily signed, and the content is contrary to the various people's organizations, and the industry has been criticized. This association deliberates and considers that there are still things that must be solemnly reported to the country. The Shanghai War and the Northeast issue should be resolved in combination, as a major policy for our foreign affairs. The people advocate in the front, and the government pledges in the back. Now the authorities intend to seek temporary peace, and suddenly stop the Shanghai war alone so that the enemy can devote all its strength to the Northeast. The ink of the signature has not dried, and the beacon of Yuguan has risen. It is clear from the facts that the overall situation has been defeated. Moreover, the government has repeatedly stated that the ceasefire agreement does not involve political clauses, but according to Article 2 of the agreement, our country's troops will temporarily stay in their current positions until a method for restoring normalcy is determined. This is tantamount to establishing a guarantee for future political clauses, and even in terms of the present, this provision is equivalent to setting up a temporary non-military zone, so how is it different from a political clause? This is the big picture, deceiving the country and the people, and there is no way to conceal it. If the government authorities still know their political responsibility, they should have dealt with it themselves long ago, and not wait for the serious indignation of the people. In addition, all important international matters must be decided by the Legislative Yuan, as clearly stipulated in Article 29 of the National Government Organization Law. The content of the Shanghai Ceasefire Agreement is of great importance, and in addition to the Chinese representative and the Japanese minister signing it, the ambassadors of the Four Allied Nations also signed it. In fact, in form and substance, it is clearly an important international agreement without any doubt. Even if the Executive Yuan does not allow the people to participate, it ignores the brilliant powers of the Legislative Yuan in this national law. Therefore, although the Shanghai Ceasefire Agreement has been signed, it does not have valid conditions in our current national law, and cannot be considered to have taken effect. Our country has no reason to be bound by it. This should be clearly announced. In short, Japan is violent and unyielding, and has angered the world. Russia and the United States have risen, and it is inevitable. For the sake of self-defense, our country has no choice but to quickly devote all its strength to pacifying the bandits, eliminating civil wars, completing military preparations, and jointly shoulder the great responsibility of maintaining world justice. There is no room for further hesitation, even if the Japanese repent halfway, and speak of peace with an open mind, the Northeast and Shanghai incidents must be combined to form a fair and just solution. If there is an excuse to use the national law's invalid ceasefire agreement to arbitrarily restrict our country's freedom, or to advocate opening any meeting first, then our people will never recognize it as long as they have a breath. We hereby announce this, hoping to work together. National Crisis Relief Association, Republic of China."

Reinstatement of Four District Police Stations

However, the internal equipment of the police station has been stolen and almost completely destroyed. Yesterday, patrol officer Ma and others ordered craftsmen to start tidying up, and the police officers have resumed their posts as usual.

Zhabei Refugees 150

Couple Commits Suicide by Drowning in Suzhou

Left a Will That Is Too Painful to Read

A special dispatch from Suzhou on the 19th stated that Mr. Qian Junyi and his wife Zhao Pinfang, residents of Zhongxing Road in Zhabei, suffered disaster this time, with their entire family being killed. Only they themselves escaped to Suzhou. Yesterday, they both drowned in the river at Qian Wanli Bridge in Suzhou Railway Station. This morning, they were found, reportedly still embracing each other. The court conducted an inquest at 4 p.m. The will was a thousand words long, detailing the origins and circumstances in great detail. A special dispatch from Suzhou on the 19th stated that the original text of the will in the double drowning case read: "The Japanese bandits erupted, killing wantonly. The home of Junyi on Zhongxing Road was right in the path of destruction. Fortunately, Pinfang was suffering from liver disease, which was very serious at the time, and they rented another house on Route Lafayette in the French Concession, seeking safety and medical treatment. Junyi accompanied her, and the two were spared from the disaster. However, the resentment and pain in their hearts was worse than enduring calamity. The family fortune was exhausted, and the adopted son Yu Xing, along with the nanny and six employees of the pharmacy, all died tragically. If it were not for the words 'Avenge National Humiliation' printed on the China Pharmacy National Pill, the disaster would never have been so severe. The Japanese bandits hate our resistance, so they hate even more those who can resist their business. Therefore, in addition to the Commercial Press and other cultural institutions suffering the most, the Wuzhou Pharmacy also suffered a terrible disaster. The Japanese bandits have long regarded Eastern Province medicines as the origin of Chinese domestic production, and the China Pharmacy as the initiator of raising funds for the righteous cause. There was a search for the words 'Avenge National Humiliation,' and the houses and goods were all destroyed, leading to today's utter poverty. The rise and fall of the nation is the responsibility of every citizen. Those of us who have survived the disaster should be even more vigorous. It is a pity that we are weak and unable to hold a knife to join the army and kill bandits. The good prescriptions obtained through careful research will also be lost. Unexpectedly, poverty and illness have become entangled, leading to distress and danger. We have no relatives to turn to, and our friends are scattered. Although our ambition has not been extinguished, the situation is no longer what it was. What is the use? (Omitted) Wuxian is Junyi's original place of origin, and some of his cousins have shops there. Should he go to his original place of origin, hoping to get ancestral blessing and meet his relatives, and thereby find a chance to survive? Otherwise, it would be a great fortune to die by the ancestors' tombs rather than by the swords of the Japanese bandits. So he brought his wife to Suzhou. After a day, he found that he was of upright nature, not good at inquiring, and that God did not favor him, with continuous rain and exhausted funds. There was no chance of survival. In such a predicament, what should he do? He decided not to blindly follow fate and end it all. Attached is a request to be buried next to the ancestral grave. Our great-grandfather, Lord Zhishan, had three sons: Yutian, Futian, and Houtian. Junyi's grandfather, Lord Futian, moved to Shanghai, where he gave birth to our father, Lord Lanchang, who gave birth to Junyi, also known as Huizhi. Junyi is 38 years old, and his wife Zhao Pinfang is 32 years old."

Jiangwan's Sufferers' Association Continues to Request 151

Relief for Disaster Victims and Exemption from Land Tax

Yesterday, the Jiangwan District Disaster Victims' Association submitted a document to the Municipal Government, stating, "Submitting a request for prompt relief for the disaster victims in our district and exemption from this year's land tax and past arrears, we respectfully request your approval. We believe that during this Japanese invasion, our district became the center of the war, with houses turned into ruins and lives devastated. The surviving disaster victims have no way to seek survival and are in a state of utter misery. Our association previously represented all the disaster victims in the district, submitting a document and earnestly requesting exemption from this year's land tax and past arrears, so as to allow the remaining survivors to breathe. We have now read in the newspapers that the provincial government has allocated 300,000 yuan in cash to the disaster-stricken counties under the province to prepare for emergency relief, and that counties such as Tai, Jia, and Bao have already scheduled relief. The disaster situation in our district is extremely severe, unprecedented in ancient times, and relief is urgently needed. This should be carefully considered. We believe that the disaster victims in our district sacrificed their lives and fortunes for the country during the war without complaint, understanding that the order in the rear must be in good order during a long-term resistance. Now that the withdrawal of troops has been agreed upon and the accommodation has ended, the disaster victims in our district will have to return to their homeland, and the so-called clothing, food, and shelter are all gone. If the assistance is delayed, we cannot help but worry about the future. Therefore, we dare to continue requesting that a method be promptly determined to provide full relief. Secondly, according to the investigation by our association, the war losses in our district, for which there are records, include more than 500 deaths and 7,600 houses burned down. The cries of ghosts in the wilderness and the wails of people on the roads are a scene too tragic for human beings to bear. Reports indicate that the Municipal Land Bureau is urging the payment of winter grain, and notices of the temporary suspension of land sales in the war zone have been issued one after another. If the land tax in our district is not exempted, the farmers after the disaster, in addition to their own bodies, have nothing else. Even if they want to sell their fields and houses at the lowest price to pay the grain, it is impossible. Therefore, we dare to continue requesting that an order be issued to exempt this year's land tax and past arrears in our district. Based on the above reasons, we dare to submit another document to the senior officials, urgently requesting your approval to extend the last breath of the disaster victims. We are in a state of anxiety and trepidation, awaiting your orders."

The Tragic Death of a Female Corpse on Hanzhong Road 154

The Fengyu Lane on Hanzhong Road in Zhabei originally had more than 40 houses. Recently, the landlords of the lane, seeing that the Japanese army had withdrawn, had most of the residents move back. However, the lane was filled with accumulated dust and overflowing sewage. To facilitate residents' access and maintain public health, yesterday morning (the 19th), four workers were hired to clear the lane of filth. Suddenly, at around 4:00 pm, they seemed to feel something blocking the ditch. They opened the ditch cover in front of house number 23 in the lane and were shocked to find a female corpse lying face up inside. As the hole was small, they could not immediately lift it out. Upon inspection, the corpse seemed to be wearing black clothes with a flannel undershirt. The breasts and nose were already severely decayed. There was a gold tooth inlaid in the upper neck, and a hemp rope was tied around the neck. The whole body was covered with mud and was abnormally swollen, making it impossible to identify. Residents from near and far came to watch the spectacle, and the crowds were almost overwhelming. For a time, Hanzhong Road became bustling with heated discussions and conflicting opinions. However, as the corpse had been dead for many days, the foul odor was overwhelming, and passersby could not help but cover their noses and pass by. Afterward, the landlord of the lane reported the matter to the Zhabei Police Station, which dispatched officers to verify the facts and immediately ordered the local bailiff to report to the local court for an inquest and further investigation.

After Public Pressure on Postal Rates 155

Slight Reduction from Today

Two Cents for Local, Five Cents for Out-of-Town

No Increase for Books and Printed Matter

According to reliable information from the Shanghai Post Office, starting from May 20th, the various postal rates within China will be revised as follows: Letters delivered locally within the jurisdiction of each post office will be 2 cents for every 20 grams. Letters mutually sent between post offices will be 5 cents for every 20 grams. Postcards mutually sent between post offices will be 2.5 cents for a single card and 5 cents for a double card. Samples will be 3 cents up to 100 grams, 7.5 cents over 100 grams up to 250 grams, 12.5 cents over 250 grams up to 350 grams, and 15 cents over 350 grams up to 500 grams. Single registration will be 8 cents, and double registration will be 16 cents. The handling fees for receipts for parcels and express mail, and for money order issuance receipts will be 8 cents (the fee for reissuing receipts will be 16 cents). The previous regulations for collecting double or triple simple fees for books, printed matter, trade contracts, etc., will all be abolished. Furthermore, the rates for Japan, Korea, the Kwantung Leased Territory, and Taiwan will be the same as the above-mentioned items. The postal rates for letters and postcards sent to Hong Kong and Macau will be the same.

Yangtze River Water Levels Cause Panic 156

Water Rises Twenty-Four Feet

Wuhan Builds High Embankments and Fortifies Sluice Gates

The river water in Hankou has risen twenty-four feet. The usual level is fourteen to fifteen feet, about eleven to twelve feet when receding, and never more than sixteen to seventeen feet. Last year, during the Wuhan floods, the water rose to more than thirty feet. This year, the river water receded unusually shallowly in the spring. It was not until the beginning of this month that it gradually increased. On the thirteenth and fourteenth, the water in Hankou surged to sixteen feet, and the next day it surged again to twenty feet, causing great panic. Unexpectedly, after the fifteenth, it suddenly rose four feet in twenty-four hours, reaching twenty-four feet. The upstream water also seems to be flowing downstream, and there is no telling how high it will rise.

Rushing to Build the Wutai Sluice Gate The Wutai Sluice Gate in Wuhan is the first line of defense against the water in Hankou and is the responsibility of the Public Works Bureau. Managers now face a situation where the river water in Wuhan has suddenly increased by seven or eight feet in the past ten days. The people of Wuhan, having learned a lesson from last year's floods, are all fearful. The Wuhan Water Conservancy Bureau, aware of the rapid rise in water, is preparing urgently. Since the sixteenth, it has specially assigned 800 people to rush to repair the Wutai Sluice Gate, working day and night to ensure that the sluice gate is consolidated and does not collapse.

Adding Embankments Along the Gan and Han Rivers Although the embankments along the river from Jiujiang to Hankou have been repaired, yesterday, Shanghai merchants received a telegram from Hankou stating that the water level had been rising continuously in recent days. During high tide, the river water was only one and a half to two feet away from the embankment. If it rises again, it will be as destructive as last year. Therefore, the Disaster Relief Supervisory Committee has allocated a portion of the disaster relief funds for work relief, ordering farmers along the river from Gan to Han to start work simultaneously on the sixteenth, raising the embankment to the height agreed upon during last year's flood. They have been rushing to build it day and night.
