The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Asks the Municipal Government 158

To Demand the Return of Chinese Detained by the Japanese Army

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce formally requested the Municipal Government to negotiate with the Japanese side to release all the detained Chinese. The formal request stated: "Regarding the formal request for this matter, on the 18th of this month, we received a letter from Jiang Xietai's Workshop, stating that the workshop is located in Hongkou, and after the Sino-Japanese War broke out, eight of the workshop's employees were detained by the Japanese army on January 30th. Several months have passed, and their fate is unknown. After the incident, we immediately reported it to various relief organizations in Shanghai and appealed for rescue, but to no avail. We have now heard that there are still detained Chinese who have not been released, and we are formally requesting your association to investigate according to the attached list of names and origins submitted by the workshop. Please inquire with the Japanese military authorities or other relevant agencies, check by name to see if they have been tried, and try to obtain their release. We earnestly request that you consider the painful situation of the families of the detainees and make every effort to negotiate with the Japanese side. If you can reunite the relatives, your virtue will be immeasurable. Attached is a list. We hope that you will investigate." Upon investigation, according to precedents, on the day when both sides exchange prisoners, those who were arrested due to military suspicion should also be released at the same time. The exchange of prisoners between China and Japan in Shanghai was implemented on April 15th. The Chinese arrested by the Japanese due to military suspicion should also be released at the same time. However, it has been repeatedly reported that the Public Works Department has investigated and reported that the number of missing persons still far exceeds the number of those released, with several hundred people still unaccounted for. It is speculated that the Japanese side only released those they deemed definitely not suspicious, while those suspected were still detained. However, now that the Sino-Japanese ceasefire agreement has been formally signed, those arrested due to military suspicion should be treated the same as prisoners of war. There is no reason to mutually exchange prisoners of war, but to continue to detain those suspected of military suspicion. This principle should exist after the ceasefire. Regardless of where they were arrested, whether in the concession or not, the people are ultimately Chinese citizens. Several hundred people are still missing. In addition to the eight employees of the above-mentioned workshop who were arrested, whose names are listed and attached, we formally request your government to examine and approve the matter. Please seriously negotiate with the Japanese side, and release all the Chinese arrested by the Japanese after January 28th, and return the bodies of the dead. Do not allow this matter to be dealt with vaguely, so as to value human life. Submitted to the Municipal Government, with the following list: (1) Shi Zhenqian, 52 years old, from Xiaoshuhe East, Chongming; (2) Shi Falang, 33 years old, same as above; (3) Qiu Dalang, 19 years old, same as above; (4) Gu Lansun, 24 years old, from Wanshou'an, Liuhuo North; (5) Jin Yongqi, 26 years old, from Loutang North; (6) Kunyuan, 27 years old, from Shuhe Town, Chongming; (7) Huang Xifan, 18 years old, from Xinkaihe, Chongming; (8) Zhou Zuguo, 25 years old, from Shuhe Town, Chongming."

Page 11

Niujiaojian, Pudong 160

Farmers' Corps Members Engage in Fierce Battle with Bandits

Thirteen Bandits Captured

Two Farmers Shot and Killed

On the afternoon of the 13th of this month, a large gang of 78 bandits arrived in Niujiaojian, Yuanbei Township, Nanhui County, Pudong, and engaged in a fierce battle with the local defense corps and farmers overnight. Thirteen bandits were captured (one of whom died), and two farmers were also shot and killed by the bandits. The details are as follows:

Menacing Faces Niujiaojian is a remote town with only three or five small shops. The farmers in the surrounding villages are good at bird hunting and are known for their bravery. During their leisure time, they gather in the town to play or sit in small teahouses to drink tea. Foreigners rarely pass through the area. At around 4:00 pm on the 13th of this month, a large gang of men with menacing faces suddenly arrived in the town from the Lijiaqiao area to the west, in groups of three or five, and continued eastward. In total, there were about seventy or eighty people. The farmers sitting in the small teahouse were suspicious of this situation and immediately responded to the call, grabbing their bird guns and surrounding the last batch of three people. They found a pistol and confessed that they were bandits, saying that their accomplices had all gone east. Upon hearing this, the farmers chased eastward. After about an hour, they caught five more and brought them back for interrogation.

Miserable Death of a Salt Merchant The bandits who escaped to the Huizhoudian area in the southeast, learned that eight of their accomplices had been arrested and were unwilling to give up. They waited until around 8:00 pm and then returned west to prepare to rob the arrestees. However, the police alarm had already reached the surrounding villages. A farmer named Zhang Guiqing, 55 years old, who was a salt merchant, was energetic. At the time, he was armed with a gun and ambushed on the beach west of Huizhoudian, preparing to intercept the bandits. Suddenly, he heard a lot of footsteps from the beach on the opposite side and saw electric lights shining. He immediately shouted to ask for the password. Unexpectedly, the group was a gang of bandits who shined the electric light on Zhang's body and suddenly fired seven or eight shots from Mauser pistols. The bullets hit Zhang's body, and three shots hit his waist and abdomen, causing his intestines to flow out. He immediately fell to the beach and died.

A Fierce Battle The bandits still wanted to go west, but gunshots from the surrounding villages were as dense as a string of pearls, and shouts of catching robbers were also loud. Knowing that things were not good, they ran back east. At that time, the news spread to all places, and the defense corps from Beicai, Zhangjiangzha, Changting'an, Shiyan Township, and other places sent teams to join the suppression. Seeing that there were people surrounding them from all sides, the bandits stopped near the Zhuangjia Temple, about three miles northwest of Huizhoudian, and scattered in all directions, hiding in the reed marshes and wheat fields to resist. The area was surrounded by more than 100 members of the defense corps and dozens of farmers. It was late at night, and they were shooting at each other in the dark. After a while, a farmer named Jia was shot and killed. The fierce battle lasted until midnight, and the defense corps fired more than a thousand shots, gradually advancing into the wheat fields and reed marshes. Seeing that the bandits could not resist, they broke through in the direction where the gunshots were sparse and rushed west. Four people were captured on the spot, and the main force was able to escape. The members of the defense corps followed and chased west. They pursued until about 3:00 am and captured another bandit at the Jiajiaquan area in Xilonggou. Seeing that the bandits had gone far, the members of the defense corps began to return.

Thirteen Bandits Captured A total of five bandits were captured in this battle. One bandit had several gunshot wounds and was dying. Another bandit also had several gunshot wounds, but he was still conscious because they were not critical. Two other bandits had minor injuries. That night, the defense corps took the eight bandits captured earlier by the farmers in Niujiaojian and escorted them to the Zhangjiangzha Public Security Bureau, interrogated them one by one, and then sent them to the Nanhui County Government for interrogation at dawn. One of the seriously injured bandits died before reaching the county, while one seriously injured bandit and two slightly injured bandits were sent to Gongzheng Hospital for treatment before being interrogated. It is reported that two bullets have been removed from the seriously injured bandit.

Inspection of Remains The remains of the two farmers, Zhang Guiqing and others, who died during the capture of the bandits, have been inspected by Auditor Wang Cheng, who was assigned by the county government. They were instructed to hand them over to the family members for preliminary burial, pending review. The family members of Zhang Guiqing, on the other hand, demanded generous compensation from the government because Zhang died in the line of duty, so they were unwilling to bury him. After the county government persuaded them, they agreed to bury him.

Remaining Harm from the Traitors The captured bandits all spoke with a Yangzhou accent and wore symbols issued by illegal organizations affiliated with the former Zhabei traitors. Each person had a square symbol. The weapons they carried were mainly pistols and Mauser pistols. One of the bandits was reportedly a former patrol captain of the Zhangjiangzha Public Security Bureau, who had been dismissed not long ago. The purpose of the bandits' trip, whether it was solely for robbery or if there was another motive, is still under strict investigation by the county government. The day after the incident, the members of the defense corps searched several Jiangbei boats in the nearby waters around Niujiaojian, but nothing was found.

Bureau of Social Affairs 161

Planning the Establishment of Pauper Asylums

Intended to be Implemented in Three Steps

Since assuming office, Director Mai Chaoshu of the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, in view of the fact that vagrants and beggars are rampant in the city, a phenomenon unique among the major cities of the country, which is closely related to international perception and public safety and hygiene, believes that it will be difficult to achieve results without fundamentally addressing the problem. Therefore, he consulted with Director Cai of the Bureau of Finance, who agreed to provide assistance, and planned to consult with the authorities of the two concession areas to assist in the implementation. At the same time, he instructed the head of the Fourth Section to draft a plan and budget for the pauper asylum, in order to actively implement it. Unexpectedly, the January 28th Incident erupted, and the bureau devoted all its efforts to various relief efforts, and the aforementioned plan was therefore suspended. Now that the Sino-Japanese armistice agreement has been concluded, relief work can be said to have come to an end. However, since the outbreak of the war, the city has suffered many damages, and the city treasury's income has been greatly affected. All the aforementioned plans have had to be adjusted and implemented in stages. The plan and budget draft have been submitted to the municipal government for approval. The outline of the original proposal for phased implementation is excerpted as follows:

The presentation is for the matter of requesting instructions. This city is one of the six major commercial ports in the world, connecting China and foreign countries. Celebrities from all over the world often come to China for inspection, generalizing the whole country from one corner, so international perception is particularly important. The citizens are of mixed origin, with good and bad people mixed together, and vagrants and beggars are visible everywhere, which not only hinders the appearance of the city, but also has a close relationship with public security and hygiene. According to previous reports, vagrants and beggars are a festering sore on society, with a vague organization, committing petty theft and all kinds of crimes, and are the medium of all kinds of evils. The gathering of these vagrants and beggars is due to the frequent national disasters in recent years, internal and external troubles, natural and man-made disasters, all occurring one after another. The livelihood of the people in the inland is difficult, or they regard Shanghai as a paradise, and come one after another. However, in recent years, industry and commerce have been declining, and the original businesses are already difficult to support, and many people are unemployed and find it difficult to make a living. Therefore, the number of vagrants and beggars is increasing day by day. The situation in this city is special, and police power is still difficult to unify. The police authorities find it difficult to clear up vagrants and beggars. At present, there are only two vagrant shelters run by charitable organizations, one is the Vagrant Work Practice Center in Caohejing, Nanshi, with a quota of 500 people, and the other is the Vagrant Work Practice Center on Liuying Road, Zhabei, with a quota of 350 people. With so many vagrants and beggars in this city, and only these two shelters, the disparity is so great that vagrants and beggars are everywhere in this city, becoming a phenomenon that has never existed in the major cities of the country. Since the director took office, he has witnessed the situation and his duty lies in urgently seeking remedies. He was instructing his subordinates to start planning when the January 28th Incident occurred, causing a huge wave, and he had to devote his efforts to relief work. The war destroyed the second Vagrant Work Practice Center, and the vagrants fled. After the war, the city treasury was depleted, and it was no longer what it used to be. The aforementioned plan had to be adjusted and implemented in three steps, to suit the financial resources. The first step is (A) to urge the Shanghai Charity Association to restore the second Vagrant Work Practice Center to its original state in a short period of time; (B) to urge the Shanghai Charity Association to initially expand the first Vagrant Work Practice Center and increase the number of people it can accommodate by 500. The cost of food and clothing for each person is estimated at eight silver dollars, requiring a monthly operating expense of four thousand yuan. The construction cost is proposed to be raised by the association, and the operating expenses are proposed to be allocated by the city treasury. The second step is to set up a pauper asylum in the Yinxiang area, with a temporary quota of 2,000 people. The cost of land purchase, construction, and operation will be borne by the city treasury, and the bureau will send personnel to manage it. The third step is to set up a pauper asylum in each of the southeast, southwest, and west areas of the city, each with a quota of 2,000 people. In total, the city-run pauper asylums will accommodate 8,000 people. Together with the total number of shelters run by the charity association, it will reach 10,000 people. At that time, although we dare not say that there will be no vagrants and beggars in the city, if the Chinese and foreign police authorities can cooperate and strictly arrest them, the city's appearance can be refreshed. The funds for the pauper asylums in the southeast, southwest, and west districts will be discussed with the authorities of the two concession areas after the first pauper asylum in the Zhabei district has achieved significant results. At the same time, it is proposed to levy surcharges on various taxes in the city, such as house rent, etc. If it is still not enough, then raise funds from the citizens. However, this matter is of great importance and requires a large amount of funding. We have prepared a plan for the establishment of the Shanghai Pauper Asylum, and after the first asylum has been successfully run, other urban areas can follow suit. We have attached the aforementioned plan and our humble opinions, and submit them to your Excellency for review and instruction, which would be greatly appreciated.

The first step is to instruct the Shanghai Charity Association to prepare for the restoration of the second Vagrant Work Practice Center as soon as possible: (A) investigate the losses; (B) repair the houses; (C) recruit the homeless; (D) restore the work; (E) expand the quota. At the same time, discuss with various philanthropists to expand the construction of the first Vagrant Work Practice Center and increase the number of people it can accommodate by 500 (for a total of 1,000 people including the original quota). The second step is to wait until the city treasury's income recovers after one year, and then submit a request to the municipal government to allocate funds to purchase 50 mu of land in the Yinxiang area and plan the construction drawings. At the same time, discuss assistance measures with the authorities of the two concession areas. The third step is to build the first pauper asylum and achieve significant results, and then set up a pauper asylum in each of the Nanshi, Pudong, and Huxi districts. The required expenses will be determined based on the situation at that time, and then specific measures will be considered.

Records of the Public Works Bureau Affairs 162

Public Utilities Committee Meeting. The Public Utilities Committee of the Public Works Bureau recently held a meeting. Mr. Bian Sheng proposed, and Mr. Wu Yunzhai seconded, the election of Mr. Arnold as Chairman of the Committee. Mr. An immediately stated that as the current Chairman of the Public Bus Company, if matters concerning the company are discussed in the future, another committee member should be invited to chair the meeting. This proposal was agreed to by the committee members, and Mr. An agreed to take the position of Chairman of the Committee.

Telephone Price Increase Issue. The General Office of the Public Works Bureau stated in a letter that the telephone company requested that it be allowed to increase prices from March 26th of this year, when the entire concession area was converted to automatic telephones. It was found that this matter should be discussed with the French Concession, and it was requested that staff members from the bureau be sent to consult with the French Concession and the company, as in previous cases. Another user suggested that the company's capital expenditures for the past twenty months should be reviewed before the price increase. After deliberation by the Public Utilities Committee, it was considered that if the price increase did not exceed the standards in the Ansen report, then auditing the accounts would not be necessary. The responsibility for preliminary contact could be undertaken by the General Manager and the Director of Finance, and then reported to the Committee. This proposal has been approved by the Board of Directors of the Public Works Bureau.

Water Supply Investigation Case. At a meeting of the Public Utilities Committee on May 12th, the General Manager of the Public Works Bureau reported that on December 24th of last year, the Water Supply Investigation Committee (composed of the previous Public Utilities Committee members and two additional Chinese committee members) decided to discuss Hill's report after the Director of Finance and the Director of the Three Affairs Bureau had signed it. However, the Director of the Public Works Bureau had not yet sent it. The Director of the Public Works Bureau then stated that, in his position, it was not appropriate to add criticism to Hill's expert report. However, if the Committee allowed it, he could also present his views to the General Manager's Office, but please do not regard it as criticism. This proposal was agreed to by the members. Subsequently, it was resolved that the Investigation Committee should give final consideration to the report and report to the Board of Directors on whether it can be adopted in whole or in part. This motion has been approved by the Board of Directors.

Road Cleaning Matters. The Public Works Department of the Public Works Bureau has now replaced the street sweeping and watering carts with automobiles. The water consumption last year reached more than 36 million gallons. In addition, in order to transport garbage (about 1,000 tons per day), automobiles are now also used due to the large amount of material and the long distances. Therefore, the Public Works Bureau now has five water carts, forty street sweeping carts, and twelve ditch mud carts that are no longer needed, as well as various saddle accessories, and is inviting people to purchase them.

Director Fukushima Resigns. At the Board of Directors meeting on Wednesday, Chairman Bell reported that Mr. Fukushima had resigned from his position as a Director of the Bureau due to his transfer to Tokyo, and praised Mr. Fukushima for his contributions to the Bureau's affairs. Mr. Fukushima then rose to express his thanks and hoped that the spirit of cooperation in the Bureau would continue forever, so that Shanghai would become more prosperous. The Chairman then stated that Mr. Fukushima's vacancy would be filled by a public election by the Board of Directors. It is heard that Mr. Terai Hisanobu, the manager of the Nippon Yusen Kaisha, is a person of high repute among the Japanese residents. Therefore, it was resolved to invite Mr. Terai to join the Board of Directors.

New Western School. The Education Committee of the Public Works Bureau met on May 11th to discuss the issue of building a new Western school on Yuyuan Road. The Director of the Public Works Department stated that if a school building capable of accommodating 500 students is to be built, it would not be compatible with the current temporary school building. He suggested building a two-story building that can accommodate a maximum of 350 students, at a cost of 250,000 taels. The Director of Finance agreed with this idea, but said that plans for cutting off the roof should be prepared for the possibility of adding a floor in the future. The Director of the Public Works Department then said that the possibility of adding a floor or adding a wing would be taken into account during the design. The Committee then resolved to follow the Director's proposal and request him to plan a school building that can accommodate 350 people at a cost of 250,000 taels. This proposal has also been approved by the Board of Directors. Regarding the issue of admitting Chinese students to the school, the Education Committee advocated that, after the school building is completed, Chinese students can also be admitted in special circumstances and when there are vacancies. This proposal was also approved by the Board of Directors.

Passenger Commits Suicide by Jumping into the River 163

Seal Engraved with the Words "Zhang Zhengrong"

Jumping into the River from the China Merchants Jiangtian Steamer

Gu Kenfu Law Office, 4th Floor, Huilu Building, 106 Sichuan Road, yesterday received a letter from Shen Huating, the Business Director of the China Merchants Jiangtian Steamer, stating that "When the steamer passed Nanjing this time, a passenger claiming to be Zhang Haishan committed suicide by jumping into the river, leaving behind several letters and a leather bag containing a copy of the novel 'Shenhai Fenghua', a clothes brush, a shoehorn, a silk long gown, three opera examination books, a toothbrush, a toothpaste, a wool blend pair of trousers, a felt hat, a crystal and a wooden seal, two undershirts, a towel, a bottle of camphor spirit, three socks, a jar of snow cream and red pills, an oilcloth, a pair of velvet women's gloves, a bottle of blue ink, a wool blanket, two pairs of shorts, an eyeglass case, half a bar of soap, a stone rubbing of a stele, a piece of silk shoe material, three photos of himself, a box of business cards, thirty-three copper coins, an empty cigarette box, and a pair of felt shoes. It was found that the seal was engraved with the words 'Zhang Zhengrong'. The addresses he left behind are: one is Lai Fuxin, No. 8 Jiaoting, Xin Jiekou, Changsha, to his uncle Zhang Caizhen; one is Yulongzhuang, Zhongda Street, Jiangcheng, Hunan, to his uncle Zhang Caibo; and one is Xiangzhenhao, Fengshi, Chaozhou, to his grandfather Zhang Focheng and his father Zhang Jiang." The letter to the ship's clerk, the letter to Lu Wuwei, No. 44 Zhongshan Hostel, Xin Jiekou, Nanjing, and the letter to someone called Diannan, requesting them to handle the reporting procedures, were consistent." Now, the original manuscripts of the relics and letters are stored in Gu Lawyer's Office. The situation has been reported to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and his family members are waiting to claim the relics.

Zhu Chenshi Commits Suicide by Poisoning 164

Sewing for a Living, Died from Economic Pressure

Zhu Chenshi, a 42-year-old woman from Huzhou who lived at No. 3, Xinxin Lane, Datong Road, Xinzha Road, went to Room 34 of the Qianqin Hostel on Tianjin Road alone at about 3:00 pm on the 17th of this month, secretly took opium and committed suicide. The next morning, the tea servant Yang Ashou discovered it and immediately reported it to the relevant General Patrol Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. The woman was taken to the hospital for treatment, but she died. The body was taken to the autopsy room on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, accompanied by forensic doctor Wei Ligong and secretary Wang Zuyi, went to the autopsy room to examine the body. According to the son of the deceased, Zhu Shengsan, 15 years old, who lives with relatives in Ximen and is currently studying, he only learned about his mother's suicide yesterday. He stated that his family consists of only his mother and himself, and his father has passed away. His mother usually sews clothes for a living. This time, she suddenly took poison, which he believed was due to economic difficulties. Mr. Guo then announced that the deceased Zhu Chenshi had indeed died from opium poisoning before her death. The body was handed over to the son of the deceased, Zhu Shengsan, for burial.

Zhang Baoqing, Martial Arts Expert, to Perform Soon 167

Zhang Baoqing, a world-renowned martial arts expert, and his National Development Technical Troupe, were once rumored to come to Shanghai to perform. However, more than a month has passed, and there is still no news of the location and date of Mr. Zhang's performance. According to someone close to Mr. Zhang, Mr. Zhang did not intend to perform in Shanghai this time. Mr. Zhang recently returned to China from Russia and intends to organize a purely Chinese circus. He has purchased more than 20 well-trained horses, which are still in Qingdao. Mr. Zhang plans to find a suitable location in Shanghai and then start preparing the circus. Therefore, he has politely declined all requests from theaters to perform his martial arts. Later, a certain gentleman who promoted martial arts and Mr. Zhang became very close. In view of the daily pressure from foreign powers, he believed that if the Chinese people want to strengthen their physique, the promotion of martial arts is urgent. If Mr. Zhang has amazing skills and does not show them to the public, it will not only bury a good method, but also hinder the promotion of martial arts. Therefore, he urgently begged Mr. Zhang to perform. Now, Mr. Zhang has agreed and is scheduled to perform for three days at the Summer Peck Theater starting next Thursday.

Pay Attention When Riding the Tram 168

Chen Zhongchang Falls off the Platform and Dies

Chen Zhongchang, a 24-year-old man from Ningbo, took Tram No. 39 on Line 6 of the French Tramway Company in the Lujiawan area of the French Concession on the afternoon of the 18th to the 16th Pier. Because there were many people, he stood on the platform outside the car. When the car passed the intersection of Xujiahui Road and Caishi Road, somehow the tram door suddenly opened, causing Chen to fall off the car and faint. The car stopped immediately, and the driver and conductor tried to revive him and sent him to Guangci Hospital for treatment. At the same time, they recorded the number and reported it to the patrolman. Chen suffered a severe head injury and died in the hospital that night after ineffective treatment. The hospital notified the police station, and the body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Autopsy Room. Yesterday, the Vehicle Department reported to the Second Special Court, and Prosecutor Wu accompanied the forensic doctor to the autopsy room to examine the body. The family member, Chen Fang, from the same clan, arrived and stated that the family members were currently in their hometown and had been notified by telegram. He could take responsibility for collecting the body. The official announced that Chen Zhongchang had indeed died from injuries sustained from the fall before his death. The body was allowed to be collected and buried by Chen Fang after signing a guarantee.

Verdict Announced in the Red Pill Smuggling Case 169

Boy from Ningbo Acquitted and Released

A Zhou family in No. 60 Ximen Road, French Concession, privately set up a red pill manufacturing facility. Between the 11th and 13th of this month, they used a boy from Ningbo, Xu Jincheng, to falsely claim that he was sending 62 packages of printed matter from the Shanghai Huibao Bookstore, containing more than 100,000 red pills, to the General Post Office on North Sichuan Road for delivery to Xuzhou. This was discovered by Gao, the postal inspector of the post office, who reported it to the Hongkou Police Station. Chinese Detective Shi Enjian and Western Detective Hai Er went to arrest the Xu boy. After questioning, they learned that Lou Zhitian from Nanjing, who was among the packages at the General Post Office, and Liu Desheng, a local hired hand at the Xiafei Road branch in the French Concession, were both accomplices. They then arrested Lou and Liu. The main culprit, Zhou, could not be found. The police station sent Lou, Liu, and the Xu boy to the First Special District Court for interrogation. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. The debate has concluded, and the verdict is awaited. Yesterday morning, the case reached the date for the verdict to be announced. Lawyer Liang Bohua, representing the Xu boy, also waited at the Gao Yi Court for instructions. Judge Qiao Wanxuan presided over the court and ruled that Lou Zhitian was sentenced to one year of imprisonment and a fine of 600 yuan for the crime of intending to sell and jointly transport opium substitutes. Liu Desheng was sentenced to two years of imprisonment and a fine of 1,000 yuan for the crime of intending to sell and jointly transport opium substitutes. If the fine is commuted to imprisonment, it will be calculated at a rate of three yuan per day. Before the judgment is finalized, the number of days of detention will be deducted from the imprisonment at a rate of two days per day. The 62 packages of red pills were confiscated. Xu Jincheng was found not guilty. Lawyer Zhang of the police station waived the appeal, and he was released immediately.

Important News

Jiangsu Department of Education 175

Improving Social Education in Various Counties

The principle of the organization is to use fewer personnel to do more work.

The focus of the work is literacy education and livelihood education.

Jiangsu's social education has been painstakingly developed over the past few years, and a basic framework has been established. After Director Zhou arrived at the Department, he actively promoted it, dividing the entire province into several mass education areas based on the autonomous regions stipulated in the county organization law. A mass education center or a farmer education center is established in each area as the central organization for implementing mass education, and implementation standards are formulated as the basis for the work. Recently, feeling that the past achievements were biased towards theoretical components and had little direct relationship with the actual life of the masses, and that the various social education organizations had failed to tighten their organizations and concentrate their efforts, another key point for the reorganization and promotion of social education in various counties has been formulated. Observing its emphasis, the principle of the organization is to use fewer personnel to do more work, and the focus of the work is literacy education and livelihood education. It is even more obvious that its plan is perfect, and the future results can be expected. The original text of its reorganization and promotion points is also attached below.

Key Points for Reorganization and Promotion of Social Education in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province

1. Social education funds in various counties must strictly comply with repeated orders and documents, and absolutely not be moved or misappropriated. 2. Various social education organizations should tighten their organizations, based on the principle of using fewer personnel to do more work. From the 21st year onwards, the standards for the distribution of funds for various organizations must uniformly comply with Article 11 of the Provisional Regulations for Mass Education Centers promulgated by the Ministry of Education, which stipulates that salary costs shall not be higher than 50%, operating expenses shall not be lower than 40%, and office expenses shall account for 10%. 3. Various social education organizations should strive to eliminate excessive expenditures and avoid facilities that do not meet the urgent needs of the masses. All service personnel should concentrate all their efforts on engaging in active work and delving into the people, so that social education organizations have a direct relationship with the actual life of the masses. 4. Various social education organizations should focus on implementing literacy education and livelihood education, striving to reduce illiteracy and improve the lives of the masses. 5. Various social education organizations should cooperate with relevant organizations in the local area. If there are agricultural improvement organizations near the farmer education center, they must especially try to contact them and jointly promote livelihood education to increase the effectiveness of both parties' work. 6. Mass schools and literacy classes should be set up as much as possible. In areas where the class system is not applicable for teaching, literacy centers and question centers should be widely established, and mobile teaching methods should be adopted to replace them. 7. Public sports fields should also conduct various recreational activities with educational meaning to attract a large number of people and enable them to benefit both physically and mentally. 8. Libraries should provide more charts on national disasters and national humiliations to arouse the excitement of the masses. 9. Various social education facilities should pay attention to the universality of various places, promote utilization, and use mobile methods such as mobile libraries and mobile lecture groups, and make good use of business equipment such as instruments, specimens, models, and sports equipment, so that they are not merely display items. 10. Various social education organizations should prepare two copies of the monthly work report form and submit them to the Bureau for verification, and add an opinion to one copy and keep it in the Bureau. One copy must be submitted to the Department for review by the Bureau before the 5th of each month, and must not be delayed. 11. The diligence and laziness of the staff of various social education organizations should be thoroughly investigated by the Education Bureau and reported to the Department at any time for commendation and punishment.

The American International Moral Friendship Association has previously donated toys to children in other friendly countries and received considerable return gifts. It now plans to donate toys to Chinese children.

Shanghai's Education After January 28 (8) Shang 177

The Municipal Bureau of Education Promulgates the Outline of Elementary School Work During the War

Teachers and Students from Colleges and Universities Join Frontline and Rear Support Work

Twelve Elementary School Training Instructions 178

To complete the plan of jointly facing the national crisis, and to achieve the long-term effects of resistance, we must engage in the training of elementary school students who are the next generation of citizens. Elementary school students who have personally experienced the Shanghai crisis and suffered oppression from the enemy, should especially have special stimulation to leave a particularly deep impression in their young minds. We see that the city's education department issued a "General Outline of Elementary School Work During the War Period" in February, which is worthy of our attention.

The Municipal Education Bureau ordered all elementary schools under its jurisdiction to say: How should teachers and students of all elementary schools in our city be inspired by the enemy's invasion of Shanghai and our army's resistance to foreign aggression? According to the fearless spirit of the Premier, we will act as a backing for our soldiers at the front. At this critical moment of national survival, we should all do our best to jointly face the national crisis, so the following general outline of work is formulated: First, hold a daily self-reflection meeting, the method is as follows: (1) Hold it every morning, half an hour before the start of classes. (2) The principal convenes faculty, staff and children to attend. (3) The ceremony is as follows: A. Perform the ceremony as usual. B. The whole body recites the patriotic creed. The patriotic creed is that an enemy is attacking our Shanghai and wants to destroy our Republic of China (1) We are willing to swear to never buy Japanese goods (2) We are willing to be the backing of the soldiers at the front. (3) We are willing for all the people of the country to unite as one. (4) We are willing to do our best to save the country (5) We are willing to die rather than be slaves of a subjugated country. C. The chairman reports on current events. D. Self-reflection, silence, and the following self-reflection: (1) If there were no troops of ours resisting the enemy in front today, could we be here in peace and stability in class? (2) Our troops are at the

National Tongji University Factory Bombed and Destroyed (Photo by Li Zunyong) 179

front line killing the enemy, how hard are they working? How should we elementary school students study hard in the rear? Are there banquets and entertainment that forget the national crisis? (3) How should we firmly remember this enemy's atrocities? E. Students automatically express their opinions on saving the country, two people each time, limited to five minutes per person. F. The chairman summarizes the students' opinions on saving the country and draws conclusions. Second, train children to be frugal in clothing and food, save money to save the country, and students in each school should set up savings boxes at home to save pocket money and put it into the savings box or deposit it in the bank. This kind of savings still belongs to the children themselves, and when necessary, it can be taken out to donate to the national crisis or used for national construction. Third, the curriculum should fully accommodate, and prepare for patriotic spirit, national consciousness and practical work. Fourth, pay special attention to physical exercise. Fifth, pay special attention to the study of the geography of the war zone and its relationship with the industry and commerce of this city. Sixth, hold exercises to avoid disasters (airplanes, bullets, poison gas, etc.) and practice first aid skills. Seventh, guard the rear and respond to the national army, police and defense forces (each school should think about its own environment, lead students, and convene student families to inform them when necessary). The above tasks should be inspected and guided by the Social Affairs Bureau at any time, in order to complete the education sector's plan to jointly face the national crisis as much as possible.

Thirteen Teachers and Students Enlist 180

Schools don't have classes, students don't study, and teachers don't teach. Logically, teachers and students can enjoy a leisurely and carefree life outside of school, enjoying the sweet freedom that is hard to come by. However, when the enemy's war drums are shaking the ground, how can they enjoy an ideal life? If you live in Shanghai during the war, you will definitely see or hear countless teachers and students busier than the bees in spring, serving in the front and rear. At least one-fifth of the university volunteers abandoned their pens and joined the army, aiming to kill the enemy and become a pillar of the country. The student volunteers in the rear are also eager to fight the enemy. Even students from Columbia University and other universities across the ocean have requested to return to China to join the army. Xu Jiaxin, a bachelor of literature from St. John's University, disregarded his family and went to the front line to serve. Countless other young people cut off their fingers to join the army. Such a tragic and enthusiastic scene is truly moving and praiseworthy. Female students from Great China University, Fudan University, and Sino-French Pharmaceutical University volunteered to take care of wounded soldiers. More than 600 students from Tongji University formed a nursing team, led by team leader Dai Ruxin, and set off for the front line on February 1. More than 180 students from Central University Medical School, Aurora Medical School, and Sino-French Medical School organized a "Wartime Medical Affairs Federation," and appointed Ren Tinggui as the team leader to go to Zhabei on February 3 to rescue wounded soldiers. Aurora University has transformed its entire school into a hospital for wounded soldiers, and all medical affairs are handled by the school's doctors. The rescue team of the University Federation and the battlefield service team of China Public School are all working enthusiastically. Shi Yixuan, a teacher from Patriotic Girls' High School and Jianguo High School, also serves as the director of medical affairs at the Pushan Hospital on Xinmin Road in Zhabei. During the smoke of war, he worked day and night to diagnose and treat wounded soldiers. For several days when traffic was cut off, he stayed in the hospital alone, working diligently. When there was no food or tea, he injected a tonic and drank beef juice to maintain his energy and continue working. When the enemy saw wounded soldiers being transported to the hospital, their planes would track them down. Often, at the critical moment of removing bullets and bandaging wounds, enemy planes would drop bombs on the hospital with a bang. To this day, you can see the walls of the hospital and the surrounding area riddled with holes like a honeycomb left by bullets. According to military experts, the mortality rate of soldiers who die from bullets on the battlefield is not high. More people die after being injured due to lack of treatment or delayed surgery than those who die in battle from bullets. Therefore, the rescue work of teachers and students is equivalent to adding many experienced reinforcements, indirectly protecting the country.

Lu Jinhou, a professor at Great China University, was originally a poor scholar. He actually rented a house at No. 570 Xujiahui Road at his own expense and opened a "Wartime School for Displaced Students." Not only did he take care of them without charging a penny, but he also invited scholars to give academic lectures in the morning and practiced wartime military training in the afternoon, just like a wartime school. The Middle School Federation, Great China Middle School, Overseas Chinese Middle School, and the Shanghai Education Circle Patriotic Federation, etc., handled refugee relief affairs in the rear. Jinrong Elementary School also funded the vaccination of refugees, distributed medicinal water and soap, and extended medical treatment, etc., treating refugees like their own children.

Almost all girls' schools are busy making masks, sewing silk cotton vests, tailoring clothes and pants, etc., to donate for military use. The Middle School Federation proposed a national salvation fund of 2,000 yuan to reward loyal and brave soldiers. Chizhi, Bowen, Minzhi, Fazheng, Minli, Jiaotong and other schools donated money to purchase telescopes, goggles, food, etc. to comfort the soldiers. The University Professors Anti-Japanese Association purchased food and sent five directors to comfort the hardworking soldiers.

The University Students' Anti-Japanese National Salvation Federation sent a telegram to university students in various countries on February 18, announcing the crimes of the enemy. University student representatives participated in inquiries from all walks of life asking why the Public Concession allowed the Japanese army to occupy the concession and stage the tragedy of killing and arson. The University Professors' Association telegraphed foreign countries to disclose the truth and asked to uphold justice. There is so much work they are doing, but I can't remember many of them for a while. Writing casually, I didn't realize the length of the article was very long. I won't repeat it anymore. In short, we see that teachers and students from various schools are so selfless and sacrificing themselves to save the country, we have to learn from Liang Qichao's old saying, "China will never perish." And please forward it to the whole country, but I am worried that China is multi-faceted, such as floods and banditry, and I am deeply afraid that transportation will be inconvenient and delivery will be difficult, and please instruct the responsible agency to contact. The Ministry of Education has already telegraphed the Chinese Embassy in Washington, explaining that the domestic transportation agencies have restored their original state, and the concerns of the association are no longer a problem, and the Department of General Education of the Ministry of Education has been designated to handle everything, and I hope to convey it.

Schools Should Purchase Historical Materials on Sino-Japanese Negotiations 182

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to all directly affiliated education institutions to purchase the historical materials on Sino-Japanese negotiations during the Qing Guangxu Dynasty at its discretion. The original order said: In order to issue orders, it was approved by the letter from the Palace Museum in Beiping. It is hereby reported that the museum has been deeply aware of the complex and important nature of Sino-Japanese negotiations. In order to find out the origin and end, and to know the present cause, we must understand the past cause. Therefore, we have collected all the documents and secret documents on Sino-Japanese negotiations from the Qing Dynasty Military Aircraft Department archives and the preserved documents in the museum, from the first year of the Qing Guangxu Dynasty, and compiled and printed them into a book according to the year, entitled Historical Materials on Sino-Japanese Negotiations during the Qing Guangxu Dynasty. Now, from the first volume to the twentieth volume, two volumes are bound into one volume, a total of ten volumes have been published, and each volume is priced at six corners of silver. However, the number of Sino-Japanese historical materials is quite large, and it is expected that many volumes can be compiled. It is now being edited and printed and will continue to be published. We have sent ten volumes of the Sino-Japanese historical materials that have been published, from Volume 1 to Volume 20, for your reference. We hereby send a letter accordingly, hoping that you will check and inform all education bureaus, universities, middle schools, elementary schools, and academic organizations under your jurisdiction to subscribe directly to the Publications Distribution Office of this museum, to strengthen public friendship, etc. It is found that the historical materials are all secret facts of Sino-Japanese negotiations during the Qing Guangxu years, which are quite useful for reference. Education and academic institutions should purchase them at their discretion. Therefore, this order is hereby issued to the said office to comply with it and to inform all its subordinates to comply with it together. This order.

Middle School Speech Competition on June 3rd 184

Organized in Cooperation by the Drug Resistance Association and the Shanghai Middle School Teachers Association

The Scope of Topics is Limited to Promoting Drug Resistance

The China National Drug Resistance Association and the Shanghai Middle School Teachers and Staff Association, in view of the fact that saving the country relies on education, and middle schools are the basic stage of education, and at this time when the national crisis is invading and the clamor for opium public sales is spreading everywhere, it is specifically scheduled to cooperate on June 3rd this year, the anniversary of Lin Zexu's memorial day, to hold a Shanghai middle school student drug resistance speech competition, in order to promote in-depth research on issues such as anti-smoking and drug resistance among middle school students, so as to lay the foundation for education and national salvation. A radio broadcasting station will be used during the speech to broadcast it across the country to spread the propaganda widely. The language is limited to Mandarin. Gold and silver medals and corresponding prizes are available to encourage and enliven the atmosphere. The detailed rules of the competition are listed below.

Competition rules (1) Purpose of the event: To promote drug resistance education so that young students can deeply understand the harm of opium drugs and automatically be inspired to work on drug resistance. (2) Eligibility: Students from middle schools in Shanghai. (3) Number of representatives: Only one per school (4) Scope of topics: Opinions and concrete measures on drug resistance. The topic can be freely designated. (5) Speech time: Limited to five minutes per person. (6) Order of speeches: The order of speeches is determined by drawing lots. (7) Competition date: June 3rd this year, that is, the anniversary of Lin Wenzhong's destruction of soil in Humen. (8) Registration date: Deadline is 12:00 noon on June 1st. (9) Evaluation criteria: Thought, structure, and tone each account for one-third. (10) Evaluators are hired from famous speakers. (10)(1) Score calculation is handled by the responsible personnel of this association. (10)(2) Prize distribution: The five schools with the most points should receive prizes with differences. (10)(3) Prize collection: (A) This association (B) Middle School Teachers Association (C) Sino-Western Drug Store (D) Welcome prizes donated by all walks of life. Unless the donor specifically designates a certain achievement speaker to donate, they will be distributed by this association as appropriate. (10)(4) Broadcasting location: Sino-Western Pharmacy on Four Horse Road. (10)(5) Registration location: Education Section, China National Drug Resistance Association, No. 4 Hong Kong Road. (10)(6) Reference books: Participants in the competition can purchase drug resistance publications worth five yuan at a price of one yuan.

Silk and Tea 205

Foreign Seed Silkworms in Nanxun Also Undergoing Changes

Early Silkworms on the Scaffolds Are Severely Affected by Thunderstorms and Rain

Nanxun has always been a famous silk area. In recent years, silkworm farmers have believed in foreign seeds (i.e., improved varieties). This year, farmers have abandoned local varieties and do not raise them. However, the weather has not been right. The climate has been cold and hot after flowering, coupled with continuous overcast and rainy days. Not only is the development of silkworms slow, but also silkworm farmers are very difficult to feed leaves. There has been quite a lot of loss in the middle of the big sleep. The early silkworms have already been on the scaffolds. Unexpectedly, the torrential rain and thunder the other day, coupled with the sultry heat, caused the silkworms on the scaffolds to stop spinning due to hearing the sound of thunder, resulting in stiff and dead silkworms. Even the late silkworms in the middle of the big sleep have also developed diseases such as vomiting black and diarrhea. This year's silkworm harvest has also been a disappointment.

Qimen Black Tea Officially Opens 206

Lower Than Last Year by 70-80 Taels

Qimen black tea, which has attracted attention from China and abroad, finally broke the deadlock of dense clouds but no rain yesterday at 5:00 PM. The first transaction was made by Zhongxinchang and Gongshengyong two tea shops with the German firm Xingcheng Foreign Company. The price of upper and middle grade goods opened at 210 taels, and the price of middle grade goods opened at 180 taels. According to the average comparison of goods prices, it was lower than last year by 70 to 80 taels. Subsequently, the British firm Jardine Matheson also continued to search for and handle goods. However, because it was late, most other traders were unable to catch up. Currently, foreign exchange rates have recovered, and the price of silver has turned down. The London-bound ship Ajax has been scheduled to depart on the 22nd, and the ship schedule is urgent. It is expected that the Qimen tea market will have a special development today.

Ma Xianglao's Four Non-Deaths 211

— Zongxian

The esteemed Ma Xiangbo, a man of great virtue and scholarship, is admired by all. Now at the age of ninety-three, his spirit is vigorous, resembling that of a man in his sixties or seventies. We can certainly wish him well for his upcoming centennial celebration. However, in his youth, Mr. Ma also faced many trials. I respectfully recount several events, purely as casual conversation.

(I) Revived from Death at Age Four: From birth, the Honorable Mr. Ma displayed intelligence. Even in his earliest attempts at speech, his words were extraordinary. At the age of four, he fell seriously ill and passed away. His father happened to be away from home. The family prepared the coffin but had not yet placed him inside. Upon returning, his father was overcome with grief, holding the child and unable to let go. Suddenly, Mr. Ma awoke as if from sleep and said, "Father, I am not dead. I must accomplish something before I die." To this day, Mr. Ma's endeavors have benefited the nation. Could this be the fulfillment of those words?

(II) Nearly Drowned at Age Nine: In the twenty-eighth year of Daoguang (1848), there was a great flood. The water rose to the rooftops. Mr. Ma, unfazed, found it amusing and sat on the upper floor, soaking his feet, wiggling his toes with delight. Suddenly, he slipped and fell into the water. His mother heard the splash and rushed over, quickly throwing him a pole. Mr. Ma grabbed it and was pulled out, gasping for air, complaining of swallowing too much water.

(III) Nearly Died from a Fall at Age Thirteen: From a young age, the Honorable Mr. Ma revered the Holy Mother. August 15th was traditionally the "Feast of the Assumption" in the church. The day before, Mr. Ma and several young classmates went to the church to help prepare the decorations in celebration. The colorful decorations in the hall were high up, and no one dared to climb. Mr. Ma, full of courage, ascended to the highest point when suddenly he, along with the ladder, toppled over. He remained unconscious for several hours. His survival was truly divine intervention.

(IV) Recovery from a Serious Illness at Age Twenty-Two: By this time, Mr. Ma had entered the Jesuit seminary at Tushanwan in Xuhui, forsaking worldly affairs. Overwork led to illness, and he refused to eat for forty days. He was on the verge of death, with little hope of recovery. His father went to see him but was stopped at the door, standing there weeping. Mr. Ma, in his sickbed, faintly heard what sounded like his father's voice. He thought to himself, "If I die, how can my poor father bear it?" In that moment, the doctor happened to come for a checkup and was greatly surprised, noting an improvement from the previous day. Alas, the recovery from his illness was likely due to this filial piety moving the heavens. After recovering, all his hair fell out, and for a year, he could not recognize the words he read. One can imagine the severity of his illness. The above was personally narrated to me by the Honorable Mr. Ma. He stroked his beard, sat upright, and spoke with great relish. It is a pity that my writing skills are insufficient to fully capture the spirit of his account.

Random Notes from Chang'an 212

— Yan Chonglou

Since the outbreak of Japanese aggression, the government, for the sake of long-term resistance, moved the capital to Luoyang and also proposed a secondary capital in Chang'an. Consequently, officials thronged the Longhai Road, and the declining Qin region suddenly showed signs of vitality. I am a native of Chang'an, and although I have been away from home for a long time, the scenery of my hometown remains in my mind. Now, I will describe what I remember for the readers.

The City Walls of Chang'an are the Second Strongest in the Country: Chang'an is a historically important place. The Zhou, Qin, and Tang dynasties all established their capitals here. The strength and grandeur of the city walls are second only to those of Beiping. The walls are more than ten zhang (about 33 meters) high and several zhang wide, allowing two carriages to drive side by side. Therefore, during the Bingyin Incident (1926), the Shaanxi army relied on them to hold out for eight months. The largest buildings within the city are the Bell Tower and the Drum Tower, with their carved beams and painted rafters towering into the clouds. These are remnants of the ancient imperial practice of ringing the bell in the morning and beating the drum at dusk. Now, the sound of the drum can no longer be heard, but the bell is still used on time. The sound of the bell is loud and clear, and can be heard throughout the city. ▲ Surrounded by Mountains, the Scenery is Beautiful: Chang'an is built on a plain, surrounded by the Zhongnan Mountains, making the scenery particularly secluded. The most famous sights are "Hua Mountain Immortal Palm," "Taibai Mountain Accumulated Snow," "Qujiang Stream Drinking," "Wild Goose Pagoda Morning Bell," "Ba River Willow Wind and Snow," "Thatched Cottage Misty Clouds," "Li Mountain Evening Glow," and "Xianyang Ancient Ferry." People in the Ming Dynasty even compiled a list of the Eight Views of Chang'an. Even now, during good days in spring and autumn, scholars and women still often rely on these poems to guide their sightseeing.

Rich in Historical Sites and Strong Folk Customs: Chang'an City has a wealth of historical sites, such as the "Ancient Artifacts Exhibition Hall," "Public Library," and "Stele Forest," which contain many inscriptions, historical records, and rare treasures. However, these are only for public viewing. The number of artifacts in private collections is also large. Local customs are simple and frugal, but people are extremely sensitive to insults. Therefore, there is a saying among the people: "Not afraid of wolves, not afraid of dogs, but afraid of insults." I remember when Kang Youwei went to Shaanxi, a grand welcoming ceremony was held in the market of Chang'an. However, soon after, Kang was expelled by those who had welcomed him for defrauding Buddhist monks. Dai Jitao once said that the people of Shaanxi lived in caves and should have the "insect" radical added to their name. The people of Shaanxi had already heard of this remark. This time, when Dai Jitao went to Shaanxi, the citizens of Chang'an, in order to avenge the insult of the "insect" radical, not only beat him up but also destroyed his car. This is also one of the interesting anecdotes amid the talk of making it a secondary capital.

World Tidbits 213

— Haike

The British Patent Office registers the patent rights for new inventions. Recently, an interesting new invention was registered: a method to cure snoring after falling asleep.

In Cheshire, England, an unemployed young man, in order to make a living, specializes in applying gold paint to people's doorknobs to enhance their appearance. He charges a penny or two each time, a very low price. People are quite receptive, and business is good every day. ▲ The largest clock in London is on the bank of the Thames River, at the New Shell Mxx Building. The clock face is twenty-five feet in circumference, and the minute hand is eleven feet six inches long. It is powered by electricity and has a pleasing sound. ▲ A famous British hygienist claims that marriage can help prolong life. If a man marries at the age of twenty-seven, he has the hope of extending his life by forty-two years. However, a single man of the same age will live five years less.

Frugal Official 214

— Fei Wenbao

The nation is in distress, and the government is vigorously encouraging the people to practice thrift in order to prepare for the needs of the resistance period. This is an important strategy for saving the country. A year or two ago, some newly rich individuals often spent money like water. Their clothing and living conditions exceeded those of the princes and nobles of the late Qing Dynasty. Their extravagance and licentiousness were fundamentally incompatible with the goals of the revolution. Mr. Sun Disan said that among the officials of the Republic of China, the one who truly practiced frugality was Zhang Nanxian, the former chairman of Zhejiang Province. He could live on two small silver coins a day. Ordinary civilians would find it difficult to live such a life. When he was in charge of Zhejiang, all his measures were based on reducing expenses. Although his political achievements are not discussed in detail, his simple and frugal lifestyle is admirable.

Quick Sketches on a Train 215

— Shancha

The Songjiang Woman: The Songjiang woman has thick, purple lips, and eyes like those of a goldfish. Sitting next to her is her son, about eleven or twelve years old. Perhaps due to heredity, his eyes and lips are exactly like his mother's. After the train passes Longhua, the rattling of the train windows is particularly loud. The train, like a wounded beast, plunges along the rusty tracks toward the green fields of early summer. At this moment, the ticket inspector begins checking tickets. The Songjiang woman, probably because her eyes protrude like those of a goldfish, spots him before anyone else. She quickly tells her son to hide behind her back, covering his feet with her clothes. The ticket inspector arrives, and the Songjiang woman pulls out a ticket for him to punch. When the train arrives in Songjiang, the woman and her son slip off the train like a wisp of smoke.

The Madwoman: The train stops in Jiaxing. Two villagers carry a young woman onto the train. The young woman's face has two rosy patches, indicating that she still possesses the beauty of youth, but her hands are tied with rope. The two men carry her onto the train and throw her onto the seat like a piglet. The young woman meekly accepts her fate. When the train starts moving, the young woman sings a simple tune and waves her hands innocently. The passengers on the train surround her, mocking her, but she continues to sing and dance. According to the villagers who are watching her, she became like this from crying over the death of her mother.

A Dispute: A military police officer finds a man wearing a military uniform and asks him where he is from. The man in uniform takes a letter from his pocket, which proves that he is on extended leave, stamped with the seal of the ×× regiment. The military police officer looks at the letter and says sternly, "××, you have already taken leave, so you have become a civilian. You are not allowed to wear a military uniform. Take it off quickly."

"Comrade, I haven't received my salary for six months. What do you want me to wear if I don't wear my uniform?"

"I don't care what you wear. Anyway, you can't wear a military uniform." The military police officer's tone becomes even harsher.

"I made this uniform myself. I have no other clothes, so I have to wear it. I will go anywhere with you."

At this point, the situation is becoming somewhat tense. Fortunately, Hangzhou is approaching, and the military police officer says, "I won't argue with you now. We'll talk when we get off the train."

The Life of Dairen (Part 2) 216

— Kaixu

Forty years ago, Mr. Dairen purchased a two-masted sailing ship named "NewsBoy." This was the beginning of Dairen Shipping.

From this humble beginning, day by day, month by month, it has grown into the Dairen Line, which holds the reins of the shipping industry in the Pacific today. Mr. Dairen first came to the Far East in 1901 and returned the following year. Later, the number of ships increased daily. Its most prosperous period was the fifteen years from 1915 to 1930. Now, it is still thriving and full of vigor. Mr. Dairen is now eighty-eight years old. The most amazing thing he has experienced in his life is the various inventions of modern science. He often says that forty years ago, if he wanted to communicate with the captain of a ship, he had to wait until the ship sailed into a port with telegraph service. Now, it is different. He can issue orders via radio at any time and receive a reply the next morning. He also often talks about Edison's first invention of the electric light. When he first heard about it in the newspaper, he absolutely did not believe it was possible and thought it was a deceptive rumor. He threw the newspaper into the wastebasket. Then he thought that Edison might not deceive his old friend, so he wrote to Edison, saying that if the news in the newspaper was not false, please send him a few first, and he would hang them in the lumberyard to see how strange they were. But Edison's reply was beyond Dairen's expectations. Edison said that if he wanted to light this lamp, he must first support it with iron wires around it and connect it to an electric current before it could emit light. When Dairen heard this, he burst out laughing, but he still did not know why. Mr. Dairen once wrote an autobiography, initially intending to give it only to relatives and friends. Later, he thought that his life's successful career might be helpful to young people, so he decided to publish it to the world. Mr. Dairen wrote in his autobiography, "I have come from poverty and humbleness to today all through hard work. People should all rise gradually from humbleness. Do not leapfrog. Do not skip grades. Their foundation will be solid. I ask myself, among the hardships suffered by young people, there are none greater than what I experienced in my childhood. I hope that young people will hear this and be inspired to fight. Do not be discouraged by small setbacks." Because Mr. Dairen did not forget his childhood hardships, he chartered a ship to his hometown of Foggike in Scotland one day. He returned and told people, "I wanted to find my old home, but there was nowhere to find it. The place has become a huge port with lumberyards everywhere. When I look at it, I see that pieces of wood are engraved with my name." Alas, Dairen, how great you are! All great men do not know the greatness of their cause. Only false great men proclaim themselves great.

Small News 217

— Zhonghuan

A tea server named Tao from Shen Bao went to the Sihang Joint Savings Society Preparation Depository to cash checks for a certain gentleman yesterday afternoon after 4 pm. There were two ten-yuan checks and one five-yuan check. Tao mistakenly thought they were all five-yuan checks and went to the cash-out area of the depository and said to the clerk, Shen Junrongsheng, "I want to cash out fifteen yuan." At the time, Mr. Shen was busy with work and did not examine them carefully. He gave him fifteen yuan. After Tao returned and gave them to the gentleman, he discovered that ten yuan was missing. However, it was already late and he did not have time to ask. The next morning, Tao went to the depository again and said to Shen, "I am a tea server from Shen Bao. I came to your bank yesterday to cash a check. After returning, I found that I was short ten yuan. I don't know if it was lost at your bank." Mr. Shen asked him about the details. His language and expression were certainly not false. He immediately gave him ten yuan and earnestly instructed him to be more careful next time. Such a person like Mr. Shen is worthy of praise.

— Master of Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter 7: Seeking an Audience with the Powerful Often Causes Generals to Fall; Imprisonment in the Prison of Love Can Turn a Jailer into a Husband.

The fifth wife then instructed Deshun, "Very well, you should thank Miss Eight for the reward. Fortunately, Miss Eight is not an outsider. If he wants a promising future, it's better to be a battalion or company commander in the army. That will depend on your promotion. Fortunately, there's no rush. We'll see what happens later." At this time, An Yutian had been living with her for three days and four nights. It was because of Li Wenxia's entanglement that he was afraid that he would still meet with Li Wenxia in private and be manipulated by Li Wenxia with some sad and affectionate words, arousing his old feelings and snatching him away from her, resulting in failure. In order to quickly determine the status of him and her as husband and wife, she forced him to draft a marriage announcement on the same day and send it to various newspapers to be published. The announcement also set the date for the third day. A simple ceremony was held at home. Close relatives and friends were not notified separately. On the day, he just made a few phone calls to gather some friends to make it lively. It happened that Wei Zhuomou had also come. She first announced to Wei Zhuomou and also asked Wei Zhuomou to be the witness. However, the matter about Li Wenxia was not concealed. She also asked Wei Zhuomou to persuade her in his spare time.
